'\t\t<div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><div class="mw-parser-output"><p>Interested in contributing content to BEMcyclopedia?  Sharing your knowledge can help BEM practitioners hone their skills and apply BEM effectively on their projects.  This section of the site will get you up to speed on how to create new pages, add to and refine existing pages, and ensure that the content is properly organized within the structure of the site.  Thanks for joining the BEMcyclopedia community!\n', '</p>\n', '<div id="toc" class="toc" role="navigation" aria-labelledby="mw-toc-heading"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" '<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Getting_Started">Getting Started</span></h2>\n', '<h3><span id="Who_can_contribute?"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Who_can_contribute.3F">Who can contribute?</span></h3>\n', '<p>Contributions may only be made by users who have created and logged into an account. <b>Currently, the site is in beta and editing rights are limited to only approved account holders but editing will be open to all users soon!</b> User edits will not go live immediately - a quality review will be performed before posting edits. This is to ensure that information has been vetted, and to limit spam on the website. Do not post anything that is copyrighted or offensive - it will be taken down immediately. Additionally, any user that posts content that is self-promotional may have the content removed or have their editing access restricted. Refer to the <a href="/wiki/Bemcyclopedia:General_disclaimer" title="Bemcyclopedia:General disclaimer">terms of use and disclaimers</a> for more information.\n', '</p>\n', '<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Creating_an_account_and_requesting_editing_rights">Creating an account and requesting editing rights</span></h3>\n', '<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Account_creation.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="/w/images/thumb/d/da/Account_creation.png/300px-Account_creation.png" decoding="async" width="300" height="80" class="thumbimage" srcset="/w/images/thumb/d/da/Account_creation.png/450px-Account_creation.png 1.5x, /w/images/thumb/d/da/Account_creation.png/600px-Account_creation.png 2x" data-file-width="1702" data-file-height="452" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Account_creation.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Create an account by clicking the link at the top right corner of this page.</div></div></div>\n', '<p>Create an account by clicking the link at the top of this page.  After you have created an account, send an email with your username to admin@bemcyclopedia.com. Our team will grant you editing rights.  \n', '</p>\n', '<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Software_neutrality">Software neutrality</span></h3>\n', '<p>Content on this site is not designed for a specific BEM software. To the extent possible, please try to create content that can generally be useful to users of a wide variety of BEM software tools.  We recognize that some images of software outputs and graphics may be specific to a particular software, so if you include these, be sure to focus your discussion on what the outputs or graphics are conveying and how this is useful to the project (rather than describing how to generate the graphic from that particular software). And also, be sure you created those graphics or have permission to post them!\n', '</p>\n', '<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Summary_of_site_organization">Summary of site organization</span></h2>\n', '<p>The website is organized into two main sections: <a href="/wiki/Learn_by_Design_Task" title="Learn by Design Task">Learn by Design Task</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Essential_Concepts" title="Essential Concepts">Essential BEM Concepts</a>.\n', '</p>\n', '<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Learn_by_Design_Task">Learn by Design Task</span></h3>\n', '<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Learn_by_Design_Task_-_Expanded_Index.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="/w/images/thumb/8/84/Learn_by_Design_Task_-_Expanded_Index.png/300px-Learn_by_Design_Task_-_Expanded_Index.png" decoding="async" width="300" height="111" class="thumbimage" srcset="/w/images/thumb/8/84/Learn_by_Design_Task_-_Expanded_Index.png/450px-Learn_by_Design_Task_-_Expanded_Index.png 1.5x, /w/images/thumb/8/84/Learn_by_Design_Task_-_Expanded_Index.png/600px-Learn_by_Design_Task_-_Expanded_Index.png 2x" data-file-width="1999" data-file-height="739" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Learn_by_Design_Task_-_Expanded_Index.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Learn by Design Task - Navigating the Index</div></div></div>\n', '<p>The main concept of this section of the site is to organize educational resources around a typical building design project窶冱 timeline.&#160; This is done by first identifying the major design phases of the project.&#160; Then, within each <b>design phase</b>, we have identified several <b>design objectives</b>, i.e., what the design team must accomplish during this phase.&#160; Finally, for each design objective, we identified the <b>BEM tasks</b> that may help to inform that specific design objective. \n', '</p><p>The main page for this section includes a navigation index organized according to this concept.  By expanding the sections of the index, one can drill down to more detailed pages related to each design phase, and detailed tutorials for the various BEM tasks.  The main index is not user-editable (it is only editable by site administrators to ensure that the site\'s organization principles are not changed).  However, user-created tutorials can be added to this index without the help of site admins.  More details on how to organize pages nicely in the index are provided in the "<a href="/wiki/Help_Guide_for_Contributing_to_BEMcyclopedia#Best_practices_-_Learn_by_Design_Task" title="Help Guide for Contributing to BEMcyclopedia">best practices</a>" section of this help guide.\n', '</p>\n', '<h4><span id="&quot;Design_Phase&quot;_Pages"></span><span class="mw-headline" id=".22Design_Phase.22_Pages">"Design Phase" Pages</span></h4>\n', '<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Design_phase_landing_page_overview.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="/w/images/thumb/b/b2/Design_phase_landing_page_overview.png/300px-Design_phase_landing_page_overview.png" decoding="async" width="300" height="204" class="thumbimage" srcset="/w/images/thumb/b/b2/Design_phase_landing_page_overview.png/450px-Design_phase_landing_page_overview.png 1.5x, /w/images/thumb/b/b2/Design_phase_landing_page_overview.png/600px-Design_phase_landing_page_overview.png 2x" data-file-width="1652" data-file-height="1125" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Design_phase_landing_page_overview.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Design Phase Landing Page Overview</div></div></div>\n', '<p>Clicking on the title of any of the <b>design phases</b> in the index will bring you to a more detailed page about that particular design phase. Each design phase page begins with a short description summarizing what the design team is trying to accomplish during this phase. Then the page is divided into several sections, each of which represents a <b>design task or design objective</b> that is typically being worked on during the given project phase. \n', '</p><p>Each of the design objective sections begins with short description of the objective.  The description aims to give the reader insight into what decision the design team is trying to make.  Then, a bulleted list of <b>BEM tasks</b> is presented. These tasks are activities that a BEM practitioner can perform to help the design team carry out the specific design objective.\n', '</p>\n', '<h4><span id="&quot;BEM_Task&quot;_Pages"></span><span class="mw-headline" id=".22BEM_Task.22_Pages">"BEM Task" Pages</span></h4>\n', '<p>These are the detailed tutorials that provide guidance on how BEM practitioners can help to inform the various design tasks that occur throughout the life of a project.  These pages should clearly describe what design decision may be informed by the BEM analysis, what analysis activities should be performed, and how the information might be shared with the design team in a meaningful way.  More information about the type of information and organization of the BEM task tutorials is provided below in the <a href="/wiki/Help_Guide_for_Contributing_to_BEMcyclopedia#Best_practices_-_Learn_by_Design_Task" title="Help Guide for Contributing to BEMcyclopedia">best practices</a> section of this help page.\n', '</p>\n', '<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Essential_BEM_Concepts">Essential BEM Concepts</span></h3>\n', '<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Essential_Concepts_-_Expanded_Index.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="/w/images/thumb/e/e2/Essential_Concepts_-_Expanded_Index.png/300px-Essential_Concepts_-_Expanded_Index.png" decoding="async" width="300" height="207" class="thumbimage" srcset="/w/images/thumb/e/e2/Essential_Concepts_-_Expanded_Index.png/450px-Essential_Concepts_-_Expanded_Index.png 1.5x, /w/images/thumb/e/e2/Essential_Concepts_-_Expanded_Index.png/600px-Essential_Concepts_-_Expanded_Index.png 2x" data-file-width="1631" data-file-height="1125" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Essential_Concepts_-_Expanded_Index.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Essential Concepts - Partially Expanded Index Page</div></div></div>\n', '<p>This section is a collection of general BEM knowledge, and fundamental skills that apply to a variety of BEM tasks.  There are subsections that discuss principles of building science (how buildings work in the real world) so that modelers have a better understanding of how the models relate to these principles; there are also numerous subsections that provide guidance on how to create models at varying levels of detail depending on what stage of design the project is in; there is guidance on how to interpret simulation results (by relating the results back to the building science principles), and how to present the results effectively; and there is guidance on various time-saving approaches such as automation and scripting. Many of the "BEM tasks" in the "Learn by Design Task" section will link to additional information within the Essential BEM Concepts section of the site.\n', '</p><p>The main page for this section includes a navigation index organized by the main subsections.  By expanding the sections of the index, one can drill down to more detailed pages related to each subsection, and detailed tutorials for many concepts.  The main index is not user-editable (it is only editable by site administrators to ensure that the site\'s organization principles are not changed).  However, user-created tutorials can be added to this index without the help of site admins. More details on how to organize pages nicely in the index are provided in the "<a href="/wiki/Help_Guide_for_Contributing_to_BEMcyclopedia#Best_practices_-_Essential_BEM_concepts" title="Help Guide for Contributing to BEMcyclopedia">best practices</a>" section of this help guide.\n', '</p>\n', '<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Glossary_Pages">Glossary Pages</span></h3>\n', '<p>Some pages may just be simple definitions of BEM, design, building physics, or other terms commonly encountered by BEM practitioners.  These pages do not need to be structured and organized like in the Learn by Design Task and Essential BEM Concepts pages.  But, they are often useful to be included as links within the detailed tutorials on this site.\n', '</p>\n', '<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Editing_pages">Editing pages</span></h2>\n', '<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Editing_an_existing_page">Editing an existing page</span></h3>\n', '<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Edit_buttons.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="/w/images/thumb/d/dc/Edit_buttons.png/300px-Edit_buttons.png" decoding="async" width="300" height="150" class="thumbimage" srcset="/w/images/thumb/d/dc/Edit_buttons.png/450px-Edit_buttons.png 1.5x, /w/images/thumb/d/dc/Edit_buttons.png/600px-Edit_buttons.png 2x" data-file-width="1999" data-file-height="1002" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Edit_buttons.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Edit buttons to edit existing pages</div></div></div>\n', '<p>Editing an existing page can easily be done by clicking either the "edit" or "edit source" buttons.  If you are not logged into your account, the edit buttons do not appear. \n', '</p><p>The "edit" button lets you edit pages using a convenient editing interface with numerous formatting tools built in (similar to a word processor). The "edit source" button lets you directly edit the page\'s source code in wikitext format.\n', '</p><p>Pages can either be edited all at once, or you can edit specific sections.  The benefit of editing a specific section is that this approach allows for multiple editors to work on different sections of a single page without their edits conflicting.\n', '</p>\n', '<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Using_the_editor">Using the editor</span></h4>\n', '<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Visual_Editor_Toolbar.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="/w/images/thumb/1/1a/Visual_Editor_Toolbar.png/300px-Visual_Editor_Toolbar.png" decoding="async" width="300" height="140" class="thumbimage" srcset="/w/images/thumb/1/1a/Visual_Editor_Toolbar.png/450px-Visual_Editor_Toolbar.png 1.5x, /w/images/thumb/1/1a/Visual_Editor_Toolbar.png/600px-Visual_Editor_Toolbar.png 2x" data-file-width="2002" data-file-height="937" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Visual_Editor_Toolbar.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Visual Editor toolbar - overview of controls</div></div></div>\n', '<p>The editor (called "Visual Editor") is a feature of the MediaWiki software that lets users conveniently create and edit pages using a word processor style interface. An overview of the controls are provided in the thumbnail to the left.  More details about how to use features of the Visual Editor are provided in the sections below.  Additional help can be found on the <a href="https://www.mediawiki.org/wiki/Help:VisualEditor/User_guide" class="extiw" title="mediawikiwiki:Help:VisualEditor/User guide">MediaWiki Visual Editor user guide</a>. \n', '</p>\n', '<h4><span id="Editing_the_source_code_(wikitext)"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Editing_the_source_code_.28wikitext.29">Editing the source code (wikitext)</span></h4>\n', '<p>Pages can also be created and edited using source code in a format called wikitext.  Wikitext allows for a great deal of customization, formatting, and special controls that are not all available in the Visual Editor, however it requires a fair bit of knowledge to use effectively.  Most of the information on this help page is geared around using the Visual Editor, but there are some advanced use cases where you may wish to edit the wikitext directly such as formatting tables, or inserting "template" information.  Wikitext also includes limited support for using html tags.\n', '</p><p>Additional help can be found on the <a href="https://www.mediawiki.org/wiki/Help:Formatting" class="extiw" title="mediawikiwiki:Help:Formatting">MediaWiki Wikitext help page</a>.\n', '</p>\n', '<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Describing_your_edits">Describing your edits</span></h4>\n', '<p>When you click the button to save your edits, you will be prompted to type a short summary of what you edited.  Keep it brief (one line) but descriptive.  This will help your fellow editors see what changes have been made since they last worked on the page.\n', '</p>\n', '<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Adding_sections_to_a_page">Adding sections to a page</span></h3>\n', '<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Adding_sections_to_a_page.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="/w/images/thumb/a/a4/Adding_sections_to_a_page.png/300px-Adding_sections_to_a_page.png" decoding="async" width="300" height="161" class="thumbimage" srcset="/w/images/thumb/a/a4/Adding_sections_to_a_page.png/450px-Adding_sections_to_a_page.png 1.5x, /w/images/thumb/a/a4/Adding_sections_to_a_page.png/600px-Adding_sections_to_a_page.png 2x" data-file-width="2095" data-file-height="1125" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Adding_sections_to_a_page.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Adding sections to a page</div></div></div>\n', "<p>Sections are a nice way of organizing the contents of a page into... sections.  If sections are given meaningful titles, then readers can easily navigate the page.  Another benefit of breaking up the page into sections is that the section names appear in the page's table of contents.\n", '</p><p>To create a new section, select the desired heading level from the text style menu (refer to the thumbnail to the right). If there is already text on the line you are editing when you change the text style, then this text will become the section title.  If you are on a blank line, then any new text you write will become the section title.\n', '</p><p>Note that after "sub-heading 2", there is very little or no visual difference in lower level sub-headings.  As a general rule, try not to go "too deep" in section hierarchy as it tends to overcomplicate the contents.\n', "</p><p>Note in the image to the right that using sections will nicely organize the page's table of contents. \n", '</p><p>As a final note, one of the text styles in the drop down menu is called "page title" although you can not actually change the title of a page while in the editor.  Do not use this page title style to format other text on the page.  If you really want to rename a page, <a href="/wiki/Help_Guide_for_Contributing_to_BEMcyclopedia#Renaming_and_redirecting_pages" title="Help Guide for Contributing to BEMcyclopedia">see below</a> for guidance. \n', '</p>\n', '<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Adding_a_table_of_contents">Adding a table of contents</span></h3>\n', '<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Force_TOC.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="/w/images/thumb/6/67/Force_TOC.png/300px-Force_TOC.png" decoding="async" width="300" height="175" class="thumbimage" srcset="/w/images/thumb/6/67/Force_TOC.png/450px-Force_TOC.png 1.5x, /w/images/thumb/6/67/Force_TOC.png/600px-Force_TOC.png 2x" data-file-width="1927" data-file-height="1125" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Force_TOC.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Add a table of contents (if not added by default)</div></div></div>\n', '<p>By default, a table of contents (sometimes abbreviated to TOC) is automatically generated on a page when more than three section headings are used. If your page has fewer than 3 section headings, you can force the addition of a TOC. This is done by choosing "page settings" from the "Options menu" as shown in the thumbnail.\n', '</p><p>It is also possible to remove the table of contents from a page although this is strongly discouraged.  Some of the navigation pages have the TOC removed because navigation is designed directly into the page and the TOC is superfluous in these cases.  \n', '</p><p>As noted above, the TOC is automatically organized based on the titles of of headings and sub-headings. \n', '</p>\n', '<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Inserting_images">Inserting images</span></h3>\n', '<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Inserting_images.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="/w/images/thumb/8/83/Inserting_images.png/300px-Inserting_images.png" decoding="async" width="300" height="167" class="thumbimage" srcset="/w/images/thumb/8/83/Inserting_images.png/450px-Inserting_images.png 1.5x, /w/images/thumb/8/83/Inserting_images.png/600px-Inserting_images.png 2x" data-file-width="1999" data-file-height="1114" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Inserting_images.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Insert an image onto the page</div></div></div>\n', '<p>Images are strongly encouraged!  Graphical representations of inputs and outputs are very important to understanding BEM concepts. \n', '</p><p>When inserting images on a page, we recommend inserting them as thumbnails. They will be inserted to the right of the text section where the insertion occurred, and text will wrap around the thumbnail.  From a page layout standpoint, it is preferred to use thumbnails rather than directly inserting the full size image. Clicking on a thumbnail will still allow users to expand and view the image at full size.\n', '</p><p>To insert the image, select the option "Images and media" from the "Insert" menu. This will open a dialog box where you can either search for an image that has already been uploaded to BEMcyclopedia (e.g. if you like an image you see on another page and wish to reuse it elsewhere), or you can upload your own images.  If you are uploading your own image, you must acknowledge that it is your own work and you have the rights to share it. You can drag an image file into the upload window, or select a file from your computer.  As part of the upload process, you will be prompted to add a name to the image (usually the same as filename but if the filename is not descriptive, then give the image a meaningful name), and a description of what the image is. Finally, you will be prompted to add a caption which will appear with the image thumbnail (this caption can be changed later in the Visual Editor).\n', '</p>\n', '<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Inserting_tables">Inserting tables</span></h3>\n', '<p>The Visual Editor only has the ability to insert rudimentary tables.  This can be done by opening the "Insert" menu and selecting "Table" but the tables are very limited in terms of formatting.  If you wish to create a more visually interesting table (with highlighted cells, different colors, etc.) this can be done using the wikitext (source code) editing approach.  There are some good (and free) online tools available that let you design interesting tables using a web interface and then export the table into wikitext which you can then cut and paste into your pages source code.  Here is a good example website where this can be done: <a rel="nofollow" class="external free" href="https://www.tablesgenerator.com/mediawiki_tables">https://www.tablesgenerator.com/mediawiki_tables</a> \n', '</p>\n', '<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Linking_to_other_pages">Linking to other pages</span></h3>\n', '<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Adding_links.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="/w/images/thumb/4/48/Adding_links.png/300px-Adding_links.png" decoding="async" width="300" height="154" class="thumbimage" srcset="/w/images/thumb/4/48/Adding_links.png/450px-Adding_links.png 1.5x, /w/images/thumb/4/48/Adding_links.png/600px-Adding_links.png 2x" data-file-width="1947" data-file-height="1002" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Adding_links.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Add links to other pages</div></div></div>\n', '<p>A powerful feature of a wiki is linking to other pages on the site with related content. We strongly encourage using links within tutorials and other pages so that readers can dig deeper into related topics.  \n', '</p>\n', '<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Links_to_other_BEMcyclopedia_pages">Links to other BEMcyclopedia pages</span></h4>\n', '<p>Adding links is very easy. While in editing mode, select the text on your page that you wish to turn into a link, then select the "link" button from the toolbar.  This will pop up a window which allows you to search for the page on BEMcyclopedia that you wish to link to.  The search will automatically search for the text you highlighted, but it is possible (and often likely) that the BEMcyclopedia page name won\'t match exactly.  In this case, you may wish to search for it using other terms, or, if you already know the name of the page you wish to link to, then you can just enter it here. Note that the search feature is case-sensitive so be careful about using capital letters.  Also, note that the highlighted text in your page (that you are turning into a link) does not necessarily need to match the full name of the linked page, as long as you connect them properly.\n', '</p>\n', '<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Links_to_external_websites">Links to external websites</span></h4>\n', '<p>Adding links to external websites is very similar.  Select the text you wish to turn into a hyperlink, select the "link" button from the toolbar, then select "External site" in the pop-up window and paste the URL of the site you wish to link to.  Note that you must paste a complete URL here (including the http:// prefix).  The best way to get the full URL is by opening the page you wish to link to and copying its full URL from your browser\'s address bar.\n', '</p>\n', '<h3><span id="Adding_references/citation"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Adding_references.2Fcitation">Adding references/citation</span></h3>\n', '<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Adding_reference_list.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="/w/images/thumb/1/1d/Adding_reference_list.png/300px-Adding_reference_list.png" decoding="async" width="300" height="170" class="thumbimage" srcset="/w/images/thumb/1/1d/Adding_reference_list.png/450px-Adding_reference_list.png 1.5x, /w/images/thumb/1/1d/Adding_reference_list.png/600px-Adding_reference_list.png 2x" data-file-width="1906" data-file-height="1077" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Adding_reference_list.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Adding the References list to bottom of page</div></div></div>\n', '<p>Give credit where credit is due! If you have relied on other sources as you research a topic, be sure to add citations for all references. Citations should be added at the end of a sentence or paragraph that relies on external research materials.  If you want to know more about how/when/why to cite a source, refer to <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:Wikipedia:Citing sources">Wikipedia\'s article</a> on the topic.\n', '</p><p>To add the citation (while in editing mode), move your cursor to the point where you wish to add the citation, and select "Cite" from the toolbar. When you select the source type, a pop-up window will open that prompts you to enter information about the source such as title, authors, date of publication, etc. \n', '</p><p>If you reference a source more than once on a page, the "Cite" menu provides an option to "reuse" a previously referenced source (so you don\'t need to enter its information again).\n', '</p>\n', '<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Adding_the_list_of_references_to_the_bottom_of_a_page">Adding the list of references to the bottom of a page</span></h4>\n', '<p>If your page has citations, then you should add a list of the references to the bottom of your page.  First, create a new Heading called "References" as the last section of your page. Then, from the "Insert" menu, select "References list" and this will insert the list onto your page.\n', '</p>\n', '<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Adding_categories_to_a_page">Adding categories to a page</span></h3>\n', '<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Adding_categories.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="/w/images/thumb/f/f6/Adding_categories.png/300px-Adding_categories.png" decoding="async" width="300" height="168" class="thumbimage" srcset="/w/images/thumb/f/f6/Adding_categories.png/450px-Adding_categories.png 1.5x, /w/images/thumb/f/f6/Adding_categories.png/600px-Adding_categories.png 2x" data-file-width="1981" data-file-height="1108" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Adding_categories.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Assigning categories to a page</div></div></div>\n', '<p>The organization of this website is largely dependent on using categories appropriately. Don\'t add categories to any pages without reading that first!\n', '</p><p>To add a category, select the "hamburger" options menu and then select "Categories." If you wish to change a page\'s title, then you will actually be "moving" it to a new page address. Be careful when doing this - it is possible, and quite likely, that other pages have already linked to the original page\'s title. If you do move the page to a new address, you will be prompted whether you wish to redirect from the original title to the new title - if you do this, then page links will not break, so please do it!  However, first consider whether you actually need to rename the page in the first place.  If a page exists titled "Air conditioner", then do you really need to rename it as "air conditioning unit"? Probably not!  In many cases, it is preferable to redirect an alternate title to the pre-existing page title rather than moving the existing page to a new title.\n', '</p>\n', '<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Deleting_pages">Deleting pages</span></h2>\n', '<p>Deleting pages is disabled for all users except for administrators. Deleting is generally to be avoided as it will likely break links from other pages. Administrators reserve the right to delete any pages that are spam, or delete specific sections of spam content.  If you feel that a page needs to be deleted, please <a href="/wiki/Special:EmailUser" title="Special:EmailUser">contact the website\'s administrators</a>. (this link will open a page to send an email. Search for user name BEMAdmin and fill in the email form). Be sure to include a link for the page you wish to be deleted along with an explanation.\n', '</p>\n', '<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Editing_the_site_navigation">Editing the site navigation</span></h2>\n', '<p>As noted above in the section <a href="/wiki/Help_Guide_for_Contributing_to_BEMcyclopedia#Summary_of_site_organization" title="Help Guide for Contributing to BEMcyclopedia">summary of site organization</a>, much consideration has been put into organizing the site\'s contents into the two main groups to allow for intuitive navigation. The main <a href="/wiki/BEMcyclopedia_-_The_Energy_Modeling_Knowledgebase" title="BEMcyclopedia - The Energy Modeling Knowledgebase">homepage</a> of the site and the overview pages for <a href="/wiki/Learn_by_Design_Task" title="Learn by Design Task">Learn by Design Task</a> and <a href="/wiki/Essential_Concepts" title="Essential Concepts">Essential BEM Concepts</a> have been protected (restricted to read-only) to ensure that the site navigation remains unaltered.  However, there is still the ability to add newly created pages to the indexes (described below) so that they appear nicely organized in the overview pages. If you wish to propose changes to the protected navigation pages, see below for guidance.\n', '</p>\n', '<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Proposing_changes_to_the_site_navigation">Proposing changes to the site navigation</span></h3>\n', '<p>This website is intended to be under constant maintenance and development.  We expect that, over time, it may make sense to add new sections or make other types of modifications to the navigation.  As noted above, this functionality is currently restricted to site administrators only.  However, if you wish to propose a new section, just send an email to the user BEMAdmin using <a href="/wiki/Special:EmailUser" title="Special:EmailUser">this link</a>. Be very specific about the proposed changes.  Please note that there is nothing restricting you from going ahead and creating new pages for your desired topic area.  Feel free to create the content and organize it as you please (e.g., using a navigation page with links to your new content).  We will work with you to integrate it into the main site navigation after you have contacted us with your request.\n', '</p>\n', '<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Using_categories_properly_to_keep_site_organized">Using categories properly to keep site organized</span></h3>\n', '<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:250px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Category_Tree_-_Learn_by_design_task.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="/w/images/thumb/e/ea/Category_Tree_-_Learn_by_design_task.png/248px-Category_Tree_-_Learn_by_design_task.png" decoding="async" width="248" height="130" class="thumbimage" srcset="/w/images/thumb/e/ea/Category_Tree_-_Learn_by_design_task.png/372px-Category_Tree_-_Learn_by_design_task.png 1.5x, /w/images/thumb/e/ea/Category_Tree_-_Learn_by_design_task.png/496px-Category_Tree_-_Learn_by_design_task.png 2x" data-file-width="1999" data-file-height="1047" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Category_Tree_-_Learn_by_design_task.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Category Tree - Learn by design task. Shows the hierarchical structure, and note that pages are assigned to the lowest level of subcategory.</div></div></div>\n', '<p>As noted above in the section <a href="/wiki/Help_Guide_for_Contributing_to_BEMcyclopedia#Summary_of_site_organization" title="Help Guide for Contributing to BEMcyclopedia">summary of site organization</a>, the main overview pages for <a href="/wiki/Learn_by_Design_Task" title="Learn by Design Task">Learn by Design Task</a> and <a href="/wiki/Essential_Concepts" title="Essential Concepts">Essential BEM Concepts</a> each have a detailed index of pages, organized according to design phase (in the case of Learn by Design Task) or main subject area (for Essential BEM Concepts). These indexes are automatically generated by assigning appropriate categories to each page.\n', '</p>\n', '<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Choosing_the_right_category">Choosing the right category</span></h4>\n', '<p>Theoretically, you could assign any and all categories to a page, but then that page would appear in every section of the index and the index wouldn\'t be very useful for navigation.  There may be some cases where it makes sense for a page to appear in a couple sections, but please try to limit the number of categories assigned to the page. If you want the page to appear in both the <a href="/wiki/Learn_by_Design_Task" title="Learn by Design Task">Learn by Design Task</a> and <a href="/wiki/Essential_Concepts" title="Essential Concepts">Essential BEM Concepts</a> sections, this is also possible but make sure it really makes sense to do this.\n', "</p><p>In essence, the categories exist in a hierarchical tree structure that aligns with the website's index pages.  Familiarize yourself with these category trees as described below.\n", '</p>\n', '<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Learn_by_Design_Task_categories">Learn by Design Task categories</span></h5>\n', '<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Category_Tree_-_Essential_concepts_expanded.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="/w/images/thumb/0/09/Category_Tree_-_Essential_concepts_expanded.png/250px-Category_Tree_-_Essential_concepts_expanded.png" decoding="async" width="250" height="180" class="thumbimage" srcset="/w/images/thumb/0/09/Category_Tree_-_Essential_concepts_expanded.png/375px-Category_Tree_-_Essential_concepts_expanded.png 1.5x, /w/images/thumb/0/09/Category_Tree_-_Essential_concepts_expanded.png/500px-Category_Tree_-_Essential_concepts_expanded.png 2x" data-file-width="1560" data-file-height="1125" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Category_Tree_-_Essential_concepts_expanded.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Category Tree - expanded view of the Essential concepts tree. Expanding the tree view will show a list of all pages assigned to a subcategory.</div></div></div>\n', '<p>The <a href="/wiki/Category:Learn_by_design_task" title="Category:Learn by design task">category tree for Learn by Design Task pages can be found here</a>. The structure of the tree is identical to the index on the <a href="/wiki/Learn_by_Design_Task" title="Learn by Design Task">Learn by Design Task</a> page. It is organized first by major design phases of the project.&#160; Then, within each <b>design phase</b>, subcategories exist for <b>design objectives</b>.&#160; These <b>design objectives</b> categories are the ones you should be applying to your tutorials (aka <b>BEM tasks</b> tutorials). You\'ll note that by expanding the tree (by clicking the little arrow) will show a list of all the pages assigned to that <b>design objectives</b> subcategory. You\'ll also note that the <b>design phase</b> categories are NOT assigned to the tutorial pages. Take a moment to browse the category tree before deciding how to categorize your page.\n', '</p>\n', '<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Essential_BEM_Concepts_categories">Essential BEM Concepts categories</span></h5>\n', '<p>Similarly, the structure of the <a href="/wiki/Category:Essential_concepts" title="Category:Essential concepts">Essential BEM Concepts category tree</a> is identical to the index on the <a href="/wiki/Essential_Concepts" title="Essential Concepts">Essential BEM Concepts</a> page. It is organized according to this section of the website\'s main topic areas. As noted above, assign the lowest level subcategories to your pages to maintain the functionality of the website\'s index. The example in the adjacent thumbnail shows several tutorial pages assigned appropriately to the "Envelope Inputs" subcategory (not to the parent "Input Tutorial" category).\n', '</p>\n', '<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Experimental_categories">Experimental categories</span></h4>\n', '<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:250px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Category_Tree_-_ASHRAE_209.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="/w/images/thumb/3/33/Category_Tree_-_ASHRAE_209.png/248px-Category_Tree_-_ASHRAE_209.png" decoding="async" width="248" height="92" class="thumbimage" srcset="/w/images/thumb/3/33/Category_Tree_-_ASHRAE_209.png/372px-Category_Tree_-_ASHRAE_209.png 1.5x, /w/images/thumb/3/33/Category_Tree_-_ASHRAE_209.png/496px-Category_Tree_-_ASHRAE_209.png 2x" data-file-width="1999" data-file-height="743" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Category_Tree_-_ASHRAE_209.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Experimental <a href="/wiki/Category:ASHRAE_209_Cycles" title="Category:ASHRAE 209 Cycles">Category Tree - ASHRAE 209 Cycles</a></div></div></div>\n', '<p>There are a few experimental sets of categories being considered for future addition to the website. We have developed a category tree for designating tutorials according to ASHRAE Standard 209. In the future, we may introduce a new navigation view that lets users navigate based on the ASHRAE 209 cycles.  These categories have not been widely applied to the tutorials, but please feel welcome to do so!\n', '</p><p>Another category under consideration is user type (i.e., are the pages targeted towards architects, engineering practitioners, researchers, etc.).  If you think this would be a valuable addition, please let us know by sending an email to the user BEMAdmin using <a href="/wiki/Special:EmailUser" title="Special:EmailUser">this link</a>. \n', '</p>\n', '<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Best_practices_-_Learn_by_Design_Task">Best practices - Learn by Design Task</span></h2>\n', '<p>These tutorials are primarily focused on teaching users <u>how to apply a model for use on a specific design task</u>.  The tutorial should not teach you how to build a model, but rather how to take a model and use it to test different design options.  The nuts and bolts of how to build a model is covered in the "Essential BEM concepts" section of the website and can be referenced by many other task-specific pages.  Here is a practical example of how the content is intended to be separated between the two sections of the website.\n', '</p><p>In the <a href="/wiki/Conceptual_Design" title="Conceptual Design">Conceptual Design</a> phase, many design analysis tasks are likely to start with an early-stage, simple box model and then test different design alternatives on that model. One study may analyze different window-to-wall ratios, another may <a href="/wiki/Analyze_the_building%27s_orientation" title="Analyze the building&#39;s orientation">analyze the building\'s orientation</a>. For the example of the building orientation analysis, the tutorial page starts by telling the user to "create a simple box model" and simply providing a link to the <a href="/wiki/Simple_Box_Models" title="Simple Box Models">simple box model tutorial</a> (under the Essential BEM concepts section of the site).  Now, within the orientation analysis page the tutorial can focus on how to use that simple box model by modeling it with different rotations, shading features, etc. The tutorial should really focus on giving the user advice ("try these options," "test these parameters over this range," "consider combining this feature with another EEM," and so forth).  The simple box model tutorial can be used over and over again across many of the conceptual design tutorials, but the specific manner in which the simple box model is used and advice to the modeler is likely to vary and can be tailored for each design task analysis.\n', '</p><p>As a general rule, if you find yourself needing to explain how to model something, it should go in the "<a href="/wiki/Preparing_Model_Inputs" title="Preparing Model Inputs">Model Inputs</a>" section.  Similarly, if you find yourself needing to explain a <a href="/wiki/Building_Science_Concepts" title="Building Science Concepts">building science concept</a>, it should go in that section.  The benefit of splitting that content from the "<a href="/wiki/Learn_by_Design_Task" title="Learn by Design Task">Learn by Design Task</a>" tutorials is that it can be generalized and reused across many different tutorials by linking.  Then the <a href="/wiki/Learn_by_Design_Task" title="Learn by Design Task">Learn by Design Task</a> section can really focus on applying the knowledge to a specific design task.\n', '</p>\n', '<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Best_practices_-_Essential_BEM_concepts">Best practices - Essential BEM concepts</span></h2>\n', '<p>These tutorials are focused on teaching users basic concepts about buildings, building science, and BEM software concepts. They are not intended to teach users how to analyze specific design concepts within the building design process, but rather to give users the necessary knowledge prior to analyzing project-specific design concepts.  It is intended that these best practices will be useful to a large number of "Learn by Design Task" tutorials and therefore will be included as links within the design task tutorials.\n', '</p><p>As an example, if a "design task" analysis is being performed to analyze window to wall ratio, then links to "Essential BEM concepts" tutorials relating to how to create window geometry, how to perform parametric analysis, and building science tutorials related to window conduction and solar heat gains would be very useful to include to help users understand how to perform the design task, and how to analyze the results.  These "essential concepts" might also be useful to include for other design tasks such as shading analysis, building orientation analysis, and many others.\n', '</p><p>As a general rule, try to make the "Essential BEM concepts" tutorials as generic as possible - they should not be focused on a specific design analysis, but rather general enough to be useful in understanding many different design task analyses. In other words, keep these Essential concepts broad - if there is something that is very specific to a certain design task, then that content can go in the "Learn by Design Task" section.\n', '</p>\n', '<!-- \n', 'NewPP limit report\n', 'Cached time: 20240320191712\n', 'Cache expiry: 86400\n', 'Dynamic content: false\n', 'Complications: []\n', 'CPU time usage: 0.055 seconds\n', 'Real time usage: 0.062 seconds\n', 'Preprocessor visited node count: 165/1000000\n', 'Post窶親xpand include size: 0/2097152 bytes\n', 'Template argument size: 0/2097152 bytes\n', 'Highest expansion depth: 2/40\n', 'Expensive parser function count: 0/100\n', 'Unstrip recursion depth: 0/20\n', 'Unstrip post窶親xpand size: 0/5000000 bytes\n', '-->\n', '<!--\n', 'Transclusion expansion time report (%,ms,calls,template)\n', '100.00%    0.000      1 -total\n', '-->\n', '\n', '<!-- Saved in parser cache with key bemcyclopedia_46-mw0f_:pcache:idhash:396-0!canonical and timestamp 20240320191712 and revision id 2177\n', ' -->\n', '</div><div id="bottom-notice-ns"><table cellspacing="5" cellpadding="0" style="margin: 0em 0em 1em 0em; border: 1px solid #1DA0E7; width: 100%">\n', '<tbody><tr>\n', '<td>Content is available under the <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://creativecommons.org/licenses/by-sa/3.0/">Creative Commons Attribution-ShareAlike License</a>; additional terms may apply. '\t<a id="top"></a>\n', '\t<div id="siteNotice" class="mw-body-content"></div>\n', '\t<div class="mw-indicators mw-body-content">\n', '\t</div>\n', '\t<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">Carbon and emission metrics</h1>\n', '\t<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">\n', '\t\t<div id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Bemcyclopedia</div>\n', '\t\t<div id="contentSub"><span class="subpages"><div id="breadcrumbs2"><a href="/wiki/BEMcyclopedia_-_The_Energy_Modeling_Knowledgebase" title="BEMcyclopedia - The Energy Modeling Knowledgebase">BEMcyclopedia</a> &gt; <span id="breadcrumbs2-currentitle">Carbon and emission metrics</span></div></span></div>\n', '\t\t<div id="contentSub2"></div>\n', '\t\t\n', '\t\t<div id="jump-to-nav"></div>\n', '\t\t<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a>\n', '\t\t<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#searchInput">Jump to search</a>\n', '\t\t<div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><div class="mw-parser-output"><p>The construction and operation of buildings results in significant carbon (and other greenhouse gas) emissions impacts. Emissions may be categorized as either embodied carbon or operational carbon.\n', '</p><p>Operational carbon refers to the greenhouse gas emissions that are generated during the day-to-day operation of a building. Reducing operational carbon is typically the focus of BEM analysis and this article will focus primarily on operational carbon.\n', '</p><p>Embodied carbon refers to the greenhouse gas emissions that are associated with the production, transportation, and construction of building materials and components. This includes the energy and emissions required to extract raw materials, manufacture and transport building products, and construct buildings. Embodied carbon emissions occur before a building is operational and are therefore considered a "upfront" carbon cost.  Embodied carbon is generally analyzed via separate tools from BEM software, however BEM practitioners who are involved in other sustainability aspects of a project may participate in embodied carbon analysis as well.\n', "</p><p>Both embodied carbon and operational carbon contribute to the overall carbon footprint of a building. In fact, embodied carbon can account for a significant portion of a building's total carbon emissions, particularly for low-carbon buildings with efficient operational performance. To achieve significant carbon reductions in the building sector, both embodied carbon and operational carbon must be addressed.\n", '</p>\n', '<div id="toc" class="toc" role="navigation" aria-labelledby="mw-toc-heading"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" /><div class="toctitle" lang="en" dir="ltr"><h2 id="mw-toc-heading">Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label class="toctogglelabel" for="toctogglecheckbox"></label></span></div>\n', '<ul>\n', '<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-1"><a href="#Operational_carbon"><span class="tocnumber">1</span> <span class="toctext">Operational carbon</span></a>\n', '<ul>\n', '<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-2"><a href="#Average_emissions_factors"><span class="tocnumber">1.1</span> <span class="toctext">Average emissions factors</span></a></li>\n', '<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-3"><a href="#Hourly_emissions_factors"><span class="tocnumber">1.2</span> <span class="toctext">Hourly emissions factors</span></a></li>\n', '<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-4"><a href="#Marginal_emissions"><span class="tocnumber">1.3</span> <span class="toctext">Marginal emissions</span></a></li>\n', '</ul>\n', '</li>\n', '<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-5"><a href="#Additional_resources"><span class="tocnumber">2</span> <span class="toctext">Additional resources</span></a></li>\n', '<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-6"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">3</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a></li>\n', '</ul>\n', '</div>\n', '\n', '<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Operational_carbon">Operational carbon</span></h2>\n', '<p>Operational carbon in buildings refers to the greenhouse gas emissions that are generated during the day-to-day operation of a building. These emissions are caused by the consumption of energy for heating, cooling, lighting, ventilation, and other building services, as well as the use of appliances and equipment.\n', '</p><p>Operational carbon emissions from buildings may occur on-site via the burning of fossil fuels, such as natural gas and oil, for heating and hot water. These fuels release carbon dioxide (CO<sub>2</sub>) and other greenhouse gases into the atmosphere, contributing to climate change. Electricity consumption also generates carbon emissions, typically off-site at the power plant but sometimes on-site via running generators. The amount of operational carbon associated with the energy consumption will vary depending on the source of the electricity.\n', '</p><p>Reducing operational carbon emissions is a key part of mitigating the impacts of climate change. This can be achieved through a variety of strategies such  improving energy efficiency, using renewable energy sources, and optimizing building systems and controls. Building codes and standards may also include requirements for reducing operational carbon emissions, such as minimum energy performance standards and requirements for the use of renewable energy sources.\n', '</p>\n', '<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Average_emissions_factors">Average emissions factors</span></h3>\n', '<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Metrics-eGRID_emissions.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="/w/images/thumb/d/d0/Metrics-eGRID_emissions.png/300px-Metrics-eGRID_emissions.png" decoding="async" width="300" height="151" class="thumbimage" srcset="/w/images/thumb/d/d0/Metrics-eGRID_emissions.png/450px-Metrics-eGRID_emissions.png 1.5x, /w/images/thumb/d/d0/Metrics-eGRID_emissions.png/600px-Metrics-eGRID_emissions.png 2x" data-file-width="1931" data-file-height="970" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Metrics-eGRID_emissions.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>eGRID average CO<sub>2</sub> emissions factors by region. (Source: IBPSA-USA BEM Workshop)</div></div></div>\n', '<p>Carbon emissions factors refer to the amount of carbon dioxide (CO<sub>2</sub>) or other greenhouse gases (GHGs) that are emitted per unit of energy consumption. These factors are used to estimate the amount of carbon emissions associated with operating a building.\n', '</p><p>The average carbon emissions factors can vary depending on the type of energy source being used. For example, the carbon emissions factor for coal is higher than that for natural gas because coal has a higher carbon content per unit of energy.\n', '</p><p>According to the United States Environmental Protection Agency (EPA), the average carbon emissions factor for electricity generation in the US in 2020 was 0.957 pounds of CO2 per kilowatt-hour (kWh) of electricity generated. This includes emissions from all sources of electricity, including coal, natural gas, and renewable sources like wind and solar.\n', '</p><p>Data sources such as eGRID and others (see the Additional resources section below) report average annual emissions factors for various regions across the United States based on the mix of generation sources in each region.\n', '</p>\n', '<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hourly_emissions_factors">Hourly emissions factors</span></h3>\n', '<p>Hourly emissions factors attempt to quantify the carbon impacts of energy consumption on an hourly basis based on historical and projected grid production.  The Title 24, Part 6 energy code in California uses hourly carbon emissions factors as one of the metrics (along with another metric, TDV) to determine whether a building complies using the performance path.  The estimated energy consumption for each hour of the year is multiplied by hourly carbon emissions factors that change based on the time of day and time of year to reflect grid production profiles.\n', '</p>\n', '<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Marginal_emissions">Marginal emissions</span></h3>\n', '<p>A marginal emissions factor refers to rate at which emissions would change with a small change to electricity load.<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> These may vary significantly from average emissions factors in areas with renewable production because extra power generation to cover the marginal increase in demand may often be from natural gas power plants.\n', '</p>\n', '<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Additional_resources">Additional resources</span></h2>\n', '<ul><li>US EPA <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.epa.gov/egrid">Emissions &amp; Generation Resource Integrated Database (eGRID)</a> - a comprehensive source of data from EPA\'s Clean Air Markets Division on the environmental characteristics of almost all electric power generated in the United States.</li>\n', '<li>US EPA <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.epa.gov/climateleadership/ghg-emission-factors-hub">GHG Emission Factors Hub</a> - a regularly updated and easy-to-use set of default emission factors for organizational greenhouse gas reporting.</li>\n', '<li>NREL <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.nrel.gov/analysis/cambium.html">Cambium</a> - Cambium data sets contain modeled hourly emission, cost, and operational data for a range of possible futures of the U.S. electricity sector through 2050, with metrics designed to be useful for forward-looking analysis and decision support.</li>\n', '<li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.electricitymaps.com/">Electricity Maps</a> - API access to electricity and carbon emissions data.</li>\n', '<li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.watttime.org/">WattTime</a> - API access to electricity and carbon emissions data.</li></ul>\n', '<p><small style="color: gray">Links to external websites are provided as a convenience for further research, but do not imply any endorsement of the content or the operator of the external site, as detailed in BEMcyclopedia\'s <a href="/wiki/Bemcyclopedia:General_disclaimer" title="Bemcyclopedia:General disclaimer">general disclaimers</a>.</small>\n', '</p>\n', '<h2><span class="mw-headline" href="#searchInput">Jump to search</a>\n', '\t\t<div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><div class="mw-parser-output"><p>The process of <b>preparing model inputs</b> is similar across the different <a href="/wiki/Model_Types" title="Model Types">model types</a>: a description of the building, its constructions, and systems are entered into the simulation software. However the level of detail, scope of analysis, and source of input data will vary depending on the phase of design. Early-stage analysis may use a simpler representation of the building geometry and rely more on assumptions, defaults, or "typical" inputs, whereas later phases aim to provide inputs that are as representative as possible of actual information on the design documents.\n', '</p>\n', '<div id="toc" class="toc" role="navigation" aria-labelledby="mw-toc-heading"><input type="checkbox" Metrics</span></a></li>\n', '</ul>\n', '</li>\n', '<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-13"><a href="#Determining_Appropriate_Inputs"><span class="tocnumber">2</span> <span class="toctext">Determining Appropriate Inputs</span></a>\n', '<ul>\n', '<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-14"><a href="#Simple_Box_Models"><span class="tocnumber">2.1</span> <span class="toctext">Simple Box '</li>\n', '</ul>\n', '</div>\n', '\n', '<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Model_Input_Categories">Model Input Categories</span></h2>\n', '<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Building_Geometry">Building Geometry</span></h3>\n', '<p>The model\'s building geometry is a representation of the building\'s physical design and its surfaces such as walls, floors, roofs, windows and doors. The geometry definition will also specify which surfaces are exposed to the exterior, surfaces that are in contact with the earth (floor slabs, basements), and any features that cast shadows on the building. The level of geometry detail will vary depending on the stage of design.  Read the following tutorial for guidance on building geometry input approaches for different <a href="/wiki/Model_Types" title="Model Types">model types</a>.\n', '</p>\n', '<ul><li><b>Tutorial:</b> <a href="/wiki/Defining_the_building_geometry" title="Defining the building geometry">Define the building geometry</a></li></ul>\n', '<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Project_and_Site_Information">Project and Site Information</span></h3>\n', "<p>These inputs include general information about the building, its location, and information about site features that may impact the building's performance.\n", '</p>\n', '<ul><li><b>Tutorial:</b> <a href="/wiki/Site_conditions" title="Site conditions">Evaluate site conditions</a></li>\n', '<li><b>Tutorial:</b> <a href="/wiki/Weather_data_selection" title="Weather data selection">Weather data selection</a></li>\n', '<li><b>Tutorial:</b> <a href="/wiki/Set_the_building_orientation" title="Set the building orientation">Set the building orientation</a></li></ul>\n', '<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Envelope">Envelope</span></h3>\n', '<p>These inputs define the properties of the building enclosure (walls, windows, roofs, floors).\n', '</p>\n', '<ul><li><b>Tutorial:</b> <a href="/wiki/Define_opaque_envelope_constructions" title="Define opaque envelope constructions">Define opaque envelope constructions</a></li>\n', '<li><b>Tutorial:</b> <a href="/wiki/Define_fenestration_(glazed_constructions)" title="Define fenestration (glazed constructions)">Define fenestration (glazed constructions)</a></li>\n', '<li><b>Tutorial:</b> <a href="/wiki/Define_shading_features" title="Define shading features">Define shading features</a></li></ul>\n', '<h3><span id="Room/Zone_Information"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Room.2FZone_Information">Room/Zone Information</span></h3>\n', '<p>These inputs define how rooms and zones are occupied and operation of energy consuming equipment, and sources of internal loads within a space.\n', '</p>\n', '<ul><li><b>Tutorial:</b> <a href="/wiki/Define_internal_loads_(occupants,_lighting,_equipment)" title="Define internal loads (occupants, lighting, equipment)">Define internal loads (occupants, lighting, equipment)</a></li>\n', '<li><b>Tutorial:</b> <a href="/wiki/Define_infiltration" title="Define infiltration">Define infiltration</a></li></ul>\n', '<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="HVAC_System_Type">HVAC System Type</span></h3>\n', '<p>HVAC system input approaches can vary significantly depending on the software program being used.  System inputs may be either component-based (highly flexible, but more effort to define the system) or menu-based (predefined system types with the ability to modify some aspects of the system via menus or other options). Read more about <a href="/wiki/HVAC_system_input_approaches" title="HVAC system input approaches">HVAC system input approaches</a>.\n', '</p>\n', '<ul><li><b>Tutorial:</b> <a href="/wiki/Selecting_appropriate_HVAC_systems" title="Selecting appropriate HVAC systems">Selecting appropriate HVAC systems</a></li></ul>\n', '<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Zone_HVAC">Zone HVAC</span></h4>\n', '<p>Important zone-level HVAC inputs include outdoor air ventilation rate, thermostat setpoints and terminal unit controls. Some single zone HVAC system types are also assigned directly at the zone-level inputs or assigned directly to individual thermal zones in the model.\n', '</p>\n', '<ul><li><b>Tutorial:</b> <a href="/wiki/Ventilation_rates_-_calculations_and_inputs_for_mechanical_ventilation" title="Ventilation rates - calculations and inputs for mechanical ventilation">Ventilation rates - calculations and inputs for mechanical ventilation</a></li>\n', '<li><b>Tutorial:</b> <a href="/wiki/Define_thermostat_setpoints" title="Define thermostat setpoints">Define thermostat setpoints</a></li>\n', '<li><b>Tutorial:</b> <a href="/wiki/Define_terminal_unit_control_settings" title="Define terminal unit control settings">Define terminal unit control settings</a></li></ul>\n', '<h4><span early-stage models">Airside HVAC assumptions for early-stage models</a></li>\n', '<li><b>Tutorial:</b> <a href="/wiki/Gathering_HVAC_input_data_for_detailed_design_models" title="Gathering HVAC input data for detailed design models">Gathering HVAC input data for detailed design models</a></li></ul>\n', '<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Waterside_HVAC">Waterside HVAC</span></h4>\n', '<ul><li><b>Tutorial:</b> <a href="/wiki/Waterside_HVAC_assumptions_for_early-stage_models" title="Waterside HVAC assumptions for early-stage models">Waterside HVAC assumptions for early-stage models</a></li></ul>\n', '<h3><span id="Domestic_Hot_Water_(DHW)_Systems"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Domestic_Hot_Water_.28DHW.29_Systems">Domestic Hot Water (DHW) Systems</span></h3>\n', '<ul><li><b>Tutorial:</b> <a href="/wiki/DHW_system_assumptions_for_early_stage-models" title="DHW system assumptions for early stage-models">DHW system assumptions for early stage-models</a></li></ul>\n', '<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_Energy_End_Uses">Other Energy End Uses</span></h3>\n', '<ul><li><b>Tutorial</b>: <a href="/wiki/Other_end-uses_overview" title="Other end-uses overview">Other end-uses overview</a></li></ul>\n', '<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Specifying_Output_Details_and_Metrics">Specifying Output Details and Metrics</span></h3>\n', '<ul><li><b>Tutorial:</b> <a href="/wiki/Utility_rate_inputs_and_calculating_energy_costs" title="Utility rate inputs and calculating energy costs">Utility rate inputs and calculating energy costs</a></li></ul>\n', '<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Determining_Appropriate_Inputs">Determining Appropriate Inputs</span></h2>\n', '<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Gathering_input_data-overview.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="/w/images/thumb/b/b9/Gathering_input_data-overview.png/300px-Gathering_input_data-overview.png" decoding="async" width="300" height="151" class="thumbimage" srcset="/w/images/thumb/b/b9/Gathering_input_data-overview.png/450px-Gathering_input_data-overview.png 1.5x, /w/images/thumb/b/b9/Gathering_input_data-overview.png/600px-Gathering_input_data-overview.png 2x" data-file-width="1962" data-file-height="985" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Gathering_input_data-overview.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Sources of input data in different stages of design. (Source: IBPSA-USA BEM Workshop)</div></div></div>\n', '<p>The source of information needed to provide inputs for a model will vary depending on the stage of design and analysis objective.\n', '</p>\n', '<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Simple_Box_Models">Simple Box Models</span></h3>\n', '<p>In most cases, limited project-specific design information is available at the time when a <a href="/wiki/Simple_Box_Models" title="Simple Box Models">simple box model</a> is created. By necessity, many model inputs will be based on typical or default values. Where project-specific information is not yet available, the goal should be to develop inputs that represent typical performance and operation. &#160;\n', '</p><p>Also consider prioritizing effort on inputs that are most relevant to the design questions being evaluated. There is almost always a limited amount of time available to perform a simple box modeling exercise. If, for example, one goal of the analysis is an accurate EUI estimate, then it will be important to gather information about likely operating schedules, plug loads and any likely unusual energy end uses, because they can have a significant impact on total energy consumption. On the other hand, if the goal is to understand the relative impact of alternatives such as varying building form or window area, then generic operating schedules and internal loads may be fine. &#160;\n', '</p><p>As much as possible, the model should include project-specific inputs. Typical sources of project-specific information include documentation about the building program, owner窶冱 project requirements, and conceptual design sketches. Interviews of the owner and design team can also provide useful information on the following items.\n', '</p>\n', '<ul><li>Energy performance goals</li>\n', '<li>Expected number of occupants</li>\n', '<li>Expected operating schedule</li>\n', '<li>Building geometry constraints</li>\n', '<li>Likely presence of end uses such as exterior lighting, commercial cooking, refrigeration, computer servers or unusual plug loads.</li>\n', '<li>HVAC system preferences</li>\n', '<li>Operating data from other similar buildings, perhaps buildings occupied by the same owner</li>\n', '<li>Examples of previous projects that are being used to inform the design of the current project (if any).</li></ul>\n', '<p>Where project-specific information is not yet available, information on typical performance inputs can come from a number of sources.\n', '</p>\n', '<ul><li>Modeler experience</li>\n', '<li>Default values from software</li>\n', '<li>Energy codes</li>\n', '<li>Other references (described later below)</li></ul>\n', '<p>Regardless of the source of input information, getting the design team to review the list of assumptions is a valuable step to take before developing the model. Create a table listing important assumptions, such as envelope component performance, lighting power, plug loads, HVAC system type and efficiency, and operating schedules and setpoints. See the section Presenting an Input Summary for an example. Consider also highlighting uncertain assumptions, especially those that might have a big impact on the analysis, so the design team can prioritize their review. The review helps in a few ways. It can help the model to be a better representation of actual expected performance. It can also help get the team to start thinking about factors that affect performance.\n', '</p>\n', '<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Detailed_Models">Detailed Models</span></h3>\n', "<p>As the design progresses into the design development and construction documents phases, much more detailed information about the building's actual design will be available on the project drawings and specifications. Detailed design models will be created from information including:\n", '</p>\n', '<ul><li>Plans窶蚤rchitectural, mechanical, electrical, plumbing</li>\n', '<li>Specifications</li>\n', '<li>Basis of design document</li>\n', '<li>Sequence of operations</li>\n', '<li>Discussions with the owner and design team</li></ul>\n', '<p>The architectural drawings can provide information on building geometry and space/zone configurations, wall assembly sections, elevation drawings that indicate where different wall assemblies are used and window geometry; HVAC drawings show how the systems serve the zones, call out flow rates and equipment sizes; lighting drawings show amount of lighting installed in each space/zone and indicate power of each lighting fixture.  The project specifications can provide additional information on design setpoints, efficiency requirements, operational parameters, and sequences of control/operation for systems.\n', '</p><p>The tutorials above provide more guidance on how to gather design information and use it for the model inputs.\n', '</p>\n', '<!-- \n', 'NewPP limit report\n', 'Cached time: 20240320191709\n', 'Cache expiry: 86400\n', 'Dynamic content: false\n', 'Complications: []\n', 'CPU time usage: 0.016 seconds\n', 'Real time usage: 0.019 seconds\n', 'Preprocessor visited node count: 73/1000000\n', 'Post窶親xpand include size: 33/2097152 bytes\n', 'Template argument size: 0/2097152 bytes\n', 'Highest expansion depth: 2/40\n', 'Expensive parser function count: 0/100\n', 'Unstrip recursion depth: 0/20\n', 'Unstrip post窶親xpand size: 0/5000000 bytes\n', '-->\n', '<!--\n', 'Transclusion expansion time report (%,ms,calls,template)\n', '100.00%    1.153      1 Template:IBPSA_source\n', '100.00%    1.153      1 -total\n', '-->\n', '\n', '<!-- Saved in parser cache with key bemcyclopedia_46-mw0f_:pcache:idhash:334-0!canonical and timestamp 20240320191709 and revision id 2441\n', ' -->\n', '</div><div id="bottom-notice-ns"><table cellspacing="5" cellpadding="0" style="margin: 0em 0em 1em 0em; border: 1px solid #1DA0E7; width: 100%">\n', '<tbody><tr>\n', '<td>Content is available under the <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://creativecommons.org/licenses/by-sa/3.0/">Creative Commons Attribution-ShareAlike License</a>; additional terms may apply.
