'\t<a id="top"></a>\n', '\t<div id="siteNotice" class="mw-body-content"></div>\n', '\t<div class="mw-indicators mw-body-content">\n', '\t</div>\n', '\t<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">Conceptual Design</h1>\n', '\t<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">\n', '\t\t<div id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Bemcyclopedia</div>\n', '\t\t<div id="contentSub"><span class="subpages"><div id="breadcrumbs2"><a href="/wiki/BEMcyclopedia_-_The_Energy_Modeling_Knowledgebase" title="BEMcyclopedia - The Energy Modeling Knowledgebase">BEMcyclopedia</a> &gt; <a href="/wiki/Learn_by_Design_Task" title="Learn by Design Task">Learn by Design Task</a> &gt; <span id="breadcrumbs2-currentitle">Conceptual Design</span></div></span></div>\n', '\t\t<div id="contentSub2"></div>\n', '\t\t\n', '\t\t<div id="jump-to-nav"></div>\n', '\t\t<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a>\n', '\t\t<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#searchInput">Jump to search</a>\n', '\t\t<div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><div class="mw-parser-output"><p><b>Conceptual Design</b> is when the architect begins to define the form, scale, mass and general appearance of a building within its surrounding context.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_1-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> It can be as simple as a series of sketches, or it can be more a more detailed set of 3D models and other materials to help communicate the design vision to the client. It is typically an iterative process where the architect works with the client and other team members to refine the concepts and prepare for the latter phases of the project.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> \n', '</p><p>Sometimes architects will develop the conceptual designs during the proposal phase (before being selected by the owner) as a way to demonstrate their design philosophy and processes.  Since this work may begin before a contract is awarded, the BEM activities in this section are often performed by the architects or, an engineering or BEM consultant on the bidding team may assist the architect "at risk" to help win the project.  \n', '</p>\n', '<div id="toc" class="toc" role="navigation" aria-labelledby="mw-toc-heading"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" /><div class="toctitle" lang="en" dir="ltr"><h2 id="mw-toc-heading">Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label class="toctogglelabel" for="toctogglecheckbox"></label></span></div>\n', '<ul>\n', '<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-1"><a href="#Design_Kickoff"><span class="tocnumber">1</span> <span class="toctext">Design Kickoff</span></a>\n', '<ul>\n', '<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-2"><a href="#Establish_or_confirm_project_goals.2Ftargets"><span class="tocnumber">1.1</span> <span class="toctext">Establish or confirm project goals/targets</span></a></li>\n', '<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-3"><a href="#Assess_likely_energy_use_patterns"><span class="tocnumber">1.2</span> <span class="toctext">Assess likely energy use patterns</span></a></li>\n', '<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-4"><a href="#Design_charrettes"><span class="tocnumber">1.3</span> <span class="toctext">Design charrettes</span></a></li>\n', '</ul>\n', '</li>\n', '<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-5"><a href="#Building_Form_and_Mass"><span class="tocnumber">2</span> <span class="toctext">Building Form and Mass</span></a></li>\n', '<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-6"><a href="#Design_Features"><span class="tocnumber">3</span> <span class="toctext">Design Features</span></a></li>\n', '<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-7"><a href="#Assess_Design_Performance"><span class="tocnumber">4</span> <span class="toctext">Assess Design Performance</span></a>\n', '<ul>\n', '<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-8"><a href="#Compare_performance_to_targets"><span class="tocnumber">4.1</span> <span class="toctext">Compare performance to targets</span></a></li>\n', '<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-9"><a href="#Identify_priorities_for_improvement"><span class="tocnumber">4.2</span> <span class="toctext">Identify priorities for improvement</span></a></li>\n', '<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-10"><a href="#Assess_heating_and_cooling_loads"><span class="tocnumber">4.3</span> <span class="toctext">Assess heating and cooling loads</span></a></li>\n', '<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-11"><a href="#Assess_resilience"><span class="tocnumber">4.4</span> <span class="toctext">Assess resilience</span></a></li>\n', '</ul>\n', '</li>\n', '<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-12"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">5</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a></li>\n', '</ul>\n', '</div>\n', '\n', '<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Design_Kickoff">Design Kickoff</span></h2>\n', '<p>BEM can provide valuable information at the earliest stages of design, even before the creation of the architect窶冱 first 窶彡ocktail napkin窶 sketch. These design kickoff steps help orient the designers to a project窶冱 unique performance opportunities:\n', '</p>\n', '<h3><span id="Establish_or_confirm_project_goals/targets"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Establish_or_confirm_project_goals.2Ftargets">Establish or confirm project goals/targets</span></h3>\n', '<p>At the start of conceptual design, confirm <a href="/wiki/Set_performance_goals_for_the_project" title="Set performance goals for the project">the performance goals</a> established in pre-design. Or, if performance goals were not set during pre-design, do it now!\n', '</p>\n', '<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Assess_likely_energy_use_patterns">Assess likely energy use patterns</span></h3>\n', '<p>Identify likely patterns such as end-use energy breakdown and seasonal consumption. This information provided early in the design process can help the design team to focus efforts on high priority efficiency strategies. There are several approaches to identifying energy use patterns before a concept design has been developed.\n', '</p>\n', '<ul><li>Develop a <a href="/wiki/Simple_Box_Models" title="Simple Box Models">simple box model</a>, then <a href="/wiki/Analyzing_Model_Outputs" title="Analyzing Model Outputs">analyze the outputs</a> to find <a href="/wiki/Analysis_to_provide_answers_and_insights" title="Analysis to provide answers and insights">insights about its efficiency opportunities</a>.</li>\n', '<li>Run a <a href="/wiki/Research_performance_benchmarks#Prototype_Building_Models" title="Research performance benchmarks">prototype model</a></li>\n', '<li>Find <a href="/wiki/Set_performance_goals_for_the_project#Zero_Net_Energy_.28ZNE.29_performance" title="Set performance goals for the project">performance data for similar buildings in reference sources</a> such as ASHRAE\'s Advanced Energy Design Guides</li>\n', '<li>Find <a href="/wiki/Research_performance_benchmarks" title="Research performance benchmarks">benchmark data</a> for your building type</li></ul>\n', '<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Design_charrettes">Design charrettes</span></h3>\n', '<p>Design charrettes are interactive brainstorming sessions held early in the design or programming stages of a project. "[They] place the client and other stakeholders, as well as all or most of the professional disciplines that will contribute to the project, in the same room for, usually, one to three days." <sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> \n', '</p><p>Goals of the charrette include "kicking-off the integrated design process, reviewing project expectations, and exploring design strategies that are most appropriate to achieve a project窶冱 sustainable design goals."<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> \n', '</p><p>An "energy charrette" held early during design is one of the requirements of <a href="/wiki/ASHRAE_Standard_209-2018" title="ASHRAE Standard 209-2018">ASHRAE Standard 209</a>. Some of the required topics include determining the purpose of the BEM in the project, defining baselines, establishing perfromance metrics, reviewing benchmarks and generating a list of ECMs.  \n', '</p><p>BEM Practitioners can assist the charrette process by helping to:\n', '</p>\n', '<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Brainstorm_and_vet_ECMs" title="Brainstorm and vet ECMs"><b>Brainstorm and vet ECMs</b></a></li>\n', '<li><a href="/wiki/Using_BEM_to_support_a_charrette#Perform_pre-charrette_analysis" title="Using BEM to support a charrette">Perform pre-charrette analysis</a></li>\n', '<li><a href="/wiki/Using_BEM_to_support_a_charrette#Perform_analysis_during_the_charrette" title="Using BEM to support a charrette">Perform analysis during the charrette</a></li>\n', '<li><a href="/wiki/Using_BEM_to_support_a_charrette#Perform_post-charrette_analysis" title="Using BEM to support a charrette">Perform post-charrette analysis</a></li></ul>\n', '<p>Read more about <b><a href="/wiki/Using_BEM_to_support_a_charrette" title="Using BEM to support a charrette">Using BEM to support a charrette</a></b>.\n', '</p>\n', '<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Building_Form_and_Mass">Building Form and Mass</span></h2>\n', '<p>Massing refers to the three-dimensional shape of the building,<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> and may also be called the building\'s form.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> Decisions about the form and mass of a building can have meaningful energy impacts that are permanent (you can\'t easily retrofit the building\'s footprint), so BEM analysis in this phase is extremely important though it is often overlooked.  \n', '</p><p>BEM practitioners can assist with the following tasks:  \n', '</p>\n', '<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Compare_Massing_Options" title="Compare Massing Options"><b>Compare massing options</b></a> - If multiple massing alternatives are being considered, a model can assess their relative performance in terms of EUI, energy cost,  peak cooling load, or other metrics important to the project.</li>\n', '<li><a href="/wiki/Analyze_the_building%27s_orientation" title="Analyze the building&#39;s orientation"><b>Analyze the building\'s orientation</b></a> - determine how the building\'s orientation on the site (with respect to sun exposure and prevailing wind conditions) may impact its performance.</li></ul>\n', '<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Design_Features">Design Features</span></h2>\n', "<p>During this phase, many design features will be evaluated for inclusion in the project.  These may be structural features, features of the facade, concepts related to passive design features such as natural ventilation or daylighting, and types of active systems (e.g. HVAC, lighting) that are desirable for the project. The BEM practitioner can be instrumental in evaluating different options and demonstrating their relative performance so that the design team can make informed selections. Some options, such as HVAC system type or natural ventilation, may have some bearing on the building's form due to floor-to-floor height requirements or depth of footprint. Additionally, an assessment of thermal comfort associated with design choices can begin at this stage. \n", '</p><p>For projects that are considering multiple options of form and mass (as discussed above), some design features may perform well on one massing option but not as well on another, so it is important that design features are analyzed within that context. \n', '</p><p>BEM can be used to analyze design features in many categories:\n', '</p>\n', '<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Constructions_and_thermal_mass_options_-_conceptual_design" class="mw-redirect" title="Constructions and thermal mass options - conceptual design"><b>Constructions and thermal mass options</b></a></li>\n', '<li><a href="/wiki/Fenestration_and_daylighting_options_-_conceptual_design" class="mw-redirect" title="Fenestration and daylighting options - conceptual design"><b>Fenestration and daylighting options</b></a></li>\n', '<li><a href="/wiki/HVAC_system_options_-_conceptual_design" title="HVAC system options - conceptual design"><b>HVAC system options</b></a></li>\n', '<li><a href="/wiki/Natural_ventilation_design_features_-_conceptual_design" class="mw-redirect" title="Natural ventilation design features - conceptual design"><b>Natural ventilation design features</b></a></li>\n', '<li><a href="/wiki/Passive_solar_design_features_-_conceptual_design" class="mw-redirect" title="Passive solar design features - conceptual design"><b>Passive solar design features</b></a></li>\n', '<li><a href="/wiki/Renewable_energy_options_-_conceptual_design" class="mw-redirect" title="Renewable energy options - conceptual design"><b>Renewable energy options</b></a></li></ul>\n', '<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Assess_Design_Performance">Assess Design Performance</span></h2>\n', '<p>After the project team has developed a design concept, then BEM can be used to assess its performance. This assessment can be useful at any point during the conceptual design process. For example, it can serve as a first step before evaluating alternatives, when it can help to establish a performance baseline and highlight opportunities to explore. It can also be used to track performance compared to project goals at any point along the way. \n', '</p><p>There are some important points to keep in mind when using BEM to assess performance during early design.\n', '</p>\n', '<ul><li>There is significant unavoidable uncertainty; many inputs will be based on educated guesses about later design decisions and building operation.</li>\n', '<li>Any reporting of energy use predictions should note the uncertainty.</li>\n', '<li>Running multiple versions of the model with a range of inputs for uncertain variables (e.g. plug loads, schedules of building operation) can be useful to show how predicted energy use will vary depending on assumptions made at this stage.</li>\n', '<li>If an energy consumption prediction is desired, then extra attention from the owner and design team is needed to review model inputs and ensure that assumptions represent likely building operation.</li>\n', '<li>BEM will be most useful at this stage for comparing the relative performance of design concepts.</li></ul>\n', '<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Compare_performance_to_targets">Compare performance to targets</span></h3>\n', '<p>BEM analysis is vital to ensuring that the design is on track to meet the <a href="/wiki/Pre-Design#Project_Goals.2FTargets" title="Pre-Design">project窶冱 performance goals</a>. Knowing the current design窶冱 performance helps to inform further design decisions. While there will be uncertainty at this early stage, the BEM results are still useful as a preliminary check on design performance. The results will be especially useful for comparing how different concepts contribute to meeting targets. \n', '</p>\n', '<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Identify_priorities_for_improvement">Identify priorities for improvement</span></h3>\n', '<p>Every project is different and may have unique opportunities for improvement. Those opportunities will vary depending on factors like climate, site, building occupancy and owner preferences. BEM can be used to identify which elements of a design concept are most critical to performance and inform further conceptual design decisions. Read more about <a href="/wiki/Analysis_to_provide_answers_and_insights" title="Analysis to provide answers and insights">using BEM analysis to provide insights</a>. \n', '</p>\n', '<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Assess_heating_and_cooling_loads">Assess heating and cooling loads</span></h3>\n', '<p>Many of the decisions made during the conceptual design phase affect the heating and cooling loads that need to be met by the HVAC system. These include decisions like building form, orientation, window area, and construction types. BEM can provide a preliminary estimate of the peak heating and cooling loads for a design concept. These loads are important because they affect the size and cost of the HVAC system. \n', '</p>\n', '<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Assess_resilience">Assess resilience</span></h3>\n', '<p>Use BEM to assess a design in terms of maintaining comfort conditions when active HVAC systems are not available. BEM is most commonly used to estimate energy consumed by HVAC systems to maintain indoor comfort conditions. However, BEM can also be used to estimate indoor temperature and humidity when HVAC systems are not operating. This type of analysis could be useful to compare design concepts with, for example, different amounts of thermal mass, different levels of insulation or different natural ventilation strategies. It is important to note that this is an advanced analysis and an energy modeler performing this type of modeling should be very familiar with the calculation methods used by their simulation tool.\n', '</p>\n', '<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span></h2>\n', '<div class="mw-references-wrap"><ol class="references">\n', '<li id="cite_note-:1-1"><span lang="en">Pre-Design</h1>\n', '\t<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">\n', '\t\t<div id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Bemcyclopedia</div>\n', '\t\t<div id="contentSub"><span id="contentSub2"></div>\n', '\t\t\n', '\t\t<div id="jump-to-nav"></div>\n', '\t\t<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a>\n', '\t\t<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#searchInput">Jump to search</a>\n', '\t\t<div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><div class="mw-parser-output"><p><b>Pre-design</b> is the first phase of a design project. In this phase, the owner and architect establish design requirements and goals. Additionally, research is performed to analyze the site and local code and zoning requirements.<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> This section describes several pre-design tasks, how BEM can be used to assist in the pre-design decision-making, and data gathering activities for the BEM practitioner to apply to models in later design stages.\n', '</p>\n', '<div id="toc" class="toc" role="navigation" aria-labelledby="mw-toc-heading"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" /><div class="toctitle" lang="en" dir="ltr"><h2 id="mw-toc-heading">Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label class="toctogglelabel" for="toctogglecheckbox"></label></span></div>\n', '<ul>\n', '<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-1"><a href="#Site_Analysis"><span class="tocnumber">1</span> <span class="toctext">Site Analysis</span></a></li>\n', '<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-2"><a href="#Energy_Code_and_Program_Analysis"><span class="tocnumber">2</span> <span class="toctext">Energy Code and Program Analysis</span></a></li>\n', '<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-3"><a href="#Building_Program"><span class="tocnumber">3</span> <span class="toctext">Building Program</span></a></li>\n', '<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-4"><a href="#Project_Goals.2FTargets"><span class="tocnumber">4</span> <span class="toctext">Project Goals/Targets</span></a></li>\n', '<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-5"><a href="#Additional_Resources"><span class="tocnumber">5</span> <span class="toctext">Additional Resources</span></a></li>\n', '<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-6"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">6</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a></li>\n', '</ul>\n', '</div>\n', '\n', '<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Site_Analysis">Site Analysis</span></h2>\n', '<p>Site analysis is the study of the climatic, geographical, historical, legal, and infrastructural context of a specific site.<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> While many of these activities are performed by an architect or landscape architect, BEM practitioners can assist with the following aspects of the site analysis:\n', '</p>\n', '<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Climate_analysis" title="Climate analysis"><b>Climate analysis</b></a> - evaluate how weather conditions affect the site and help identify effective design strategies to ensure the building will be comfortable and will achieve the desired energy performance.</li>\n', '<li><b><a href="/wiki/Site_conditions" title="Site conditions">Site conditions</a></b> - evaluate how the site\'s location and surroundings may impact the design.</li>\n', '<li><a href="/wiki/Available_utilities_and_fuel_sources" title="Available utilities and fuel sources"><b>Available utilities and fuel sources</b></a> - determine if fossil fuel service is available at the site and if it\'s desired for the project or whether an all-electric design will be pursued. Determine if any clean energy electricity providers or tariffs are available for the project site if desired for the project.</li></ul>\n', '<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Energy_Code_and_Program_Analysis">Energy Code and Program Analysis</span></h2>\n', '<p>The U.S. Department of Energy\'s Building Technologies Program notes that "Energy codes affect the design of all building systems separately and collectively. Designing for energy efficiency can impact the look, feel, and function of the building. For example, lighting and window design can impact cooling loads, windows can impact lighting, and so on."<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> It is important to understand which codes apply to the project and how they, along with any beyond-code programs, may influence the design.  \n', '</p><p>BEM practitioners can assist with the following tasks:\n', '</p>\n', '<ul><li><b><a href="/wiki/Determine_the_applicable_energy_code" title="Determine the applicable energy code">Determine the applicable energy code</a></b> - identify the code and version in effect. Review mandatory requirements and the energy modeling procedures for the performance approach.</li>\n', '<li><b><a href="/wiki/Determine_ventilation_requirements" title="Determine ventilation requirements">Determine ventilation requirements</a></b> - identify the ventilation code requirements and if additional ventilation is desired by the owner.</li>\n', '<li><b><a href="/wiki/Determine_applicability_of_beyond-code_programs" title="Determine applicability of beyond-code programs">Determine applicability of beyond-code programs</a></b> - identify any additional energy modeling tasks or documentation are needed to comply with beyond-code programs (e.g. green building certifications, reach codes).</li>\n', '<li><b><a href="/wiki/Identify_potential_incentives" title="Identify potential incentives">Identify potential incentives</a></b> - identify opportunities to achieve monetary incentives associated with using energy modeling in the project design process.</li></ul>\n', '<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Building_Program">Building Program</span></h2>\n', '<p>The programming process defines how a building will be used by the occupants, including how much area will be designated for different space types.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>  Programming is typically not an activity that involves the input of an energy modeler, but the outcome of the program must be understood by the modeler as it will inform their analysis as the project progresses. \n', '</p><p>BEM practitioners should be sure to review the following aspects of the building program:\n', '</p>\n', '<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Review_space_type_percentages" title="Review space type percentages"><b>Review space type percentages</b></a> - determine approximate percentage of area associated with different space uses in the building.</li>\n', '<li><a href="/wiki/Identify_any_special_space_types" title="Identify any special space types"><b>Identify any special space types</b></a> - determine if any space types exist in the building that may need special attention given to modeling plug loads or HVAC systems.</li></ul>\n', '<h2><span id="Project_Goals/Targets"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Project_Goals.2FTargets">Project Goals/Targets</span></h2>\n', '<p>The American Institute of Architects (AIA) <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.aia.org/resources/6077668-framework-for-design-excellence">Framework for Design Excellence</a> notes that "[energy benchmarking and goal setting] is a critical first step for every project... benchmarks are easily shared with the design team and owner, and are a basis for a deeper conversation about how the building is intended to work. Everyone on the team should understand a project窶冱 benchmark and its energy goals."<sup id="cite_ref-:0_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> \n', '</p><p>BEM practitioners are often instrumental in helping to provide this understanding to the team. Their role includes:\n', '</p>\n', '<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Research_performance_benchmarks" title="Research performance benchmarks"><b>Research performance benchmarks</b></a> - review how similar building types typically perform in terms of energy use intensity (EUI), peak loads, carbon emissions, and other metrics.</li>\n', '<li><b><a href="/wiki/Set_performance_goals_for_the_project" title="Set performance goals for the project">Set performance goals for the project</a></b> - based on the benchmarking exercise, set a performance target for your project. As with the benchmarking analysis, these targets may be based on several different metrics.</li>\n', '<li><b><a href="/wiki/Determine_renewable_generation_objectives" title="Determine renewable generation objectives">Determine renewable generation objectives</a></b> - in addition to setting energy performance goals, projects may have goals for renewable energy production or procurement.</li>\n', '<li>Determine design/operation features required by owner (OPR)</li></ul>\n', '<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Additional_Resources">Additional Resources</span></h2>\n', '<ul><li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.buildinggreen.com/feature/getting-know-place-site-evaluation-starting-point-green-design">Site Evaluation as a Starting Point for Green Design</a> - Article from BuildingGreen.com describing key components of a site evaluation (beyond energy impacts).</li></ul>\n', '<p><small style="color: gray">Links to external websites are provided as a convenience for further research, but do not imply any endorsement of the content or the operator of the external site, as detailed in BEMcyclopedia\'s <a '\t\t<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#searchInput">Jump to search</a>\n', '\t\t<div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><div class="mw-parser-output"><p>Different <b>model types</b> can be useful at different stages of a project, and depending on the analysis use case. This page provides an overview of several model types. The <a href="/wiki/Learn_by_Design_Task" title="Learn by Design Task">Learn by Design Task</a> section provides further guidance on when and how to apply them.\n', '</p>\n', '<div id="toc" class="toc" role="navigation" aria-labelledby="mw-toc-heading"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" /><div class="toctitle" lang="en" dir="ltr"><h2 id="mw-toc-heading">Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label class="toctogglelabel" for="toctogglecheckbox"></label></span></div>\n', '<ul>\n', '<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-1"><a href="#Prototype_models"><span class="tocnumber">1</span> <span class="toctext">Prototype models</span></a></li>\n', '<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-2"><a href="#Simple_box_models"><span class="tocnumber">2</span> <span class="toctext">Simple box models</span></a></li>\n', '<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-3"><a href="#Shoebox_models"><span class="tocnumber">3</span> <span class="toctext">Shoebox models</span></a></li>\n', '<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-4"><a href="#Detailed_models"><span class="tocnumber">4</span> <span class="toctext">Detailed models</span></a></li>\n', '<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-5"><a href="#Compliance_models"><span class="tocnumber">5</span> <span class="toctext">Compliance models</span></a></li>\n', '</ul>\n', '</div>\n', '\n', '<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Prototype_models">Prototype models</span></h2>\n', '<p><a href="/wiki/Prototype_models" title="Prototype models">Prototype models</a> are valuable for providing a quick understanding of typical performance and for establishing benchmarks. Models of prototype buildings are available for some simulation programs, and they typically represent different building types and vintages.\n', '</p>\n', '<div class="thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Prototype_models.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="/w/images/thumb/c/c6/Prototype_models.png/300px-Prototype_models.png" decoding="async" width="300" height="152" class="thumbimage" srcset="/w/images/thumb/c/c6/Prototype_models.png/450px-Prototype_models.png 1.5x, /w/images/thumb/c/c6/Prototype_models.png/600px-Prototype_models.png 2x" data-file-width="1874" data-file-height="950" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Prototype_models.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Example Prototype Models窶禰igh-rise Apartment, Restaurant and Secondary School</div></div></div>\n', '<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Simple_box_models">Simple box models</span></h2>\n', '<p><a href="/wiki/Simple_Box_Models" title="Simple Box Models">Simple box models</a> are a type of whole building energy model used to inform early design. A simplified model is used to test the impact of fundamental design decisions on energy consumption and peak heating and cooling loads. The appropriate level of detail in the model depends on the state of the design. During pre-design, the model may look like a simple box. During conceptual design, the model will typically represent a simplified version of one or more design concepts.\n', '</p>\n', '<div class="thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Simple_box_examples.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="/w/images/thumb/6/61/Simple_box_examples.png/300px-Simple_box_examples.png" decoding="async" width="300" height="112" class="thumbimage" srcset="/w/images/thumb/6/61/Simple_box_examples.png/450px-Simple_box_examples.png 1.5x, /w/images/thumb/6/61/Simple_box_examples.png/600px-Simple_box_examples.png 2x" data-file-width="1928" data-file-height="720" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Simple_box_examples.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Example Simple Box Models窶捻re-design (left) and Conceptual Design Massing (right)</div></div></div>\n', '<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Shoebox_models">Shoebox models</span></h2>\n', '<p><a href="/wiki/Shoebox_Models" title="Shoebox Models">Shoebox models</a> represent an isolated portion of a building, such as a single representative zone. They can be useful at any stage of design to inform specific design decisions.\n', '</p>\n', '<div class="thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Shoebox_models.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="/w/images/thumb/d/d6/Shoebox_models.png/300px-Shoebox_models.png" decoding="async" width="300" height="182" class="thumbimage" srcset="/w/images/thumb/d/d6/Shoebox_models.png/450px-Shoebox_models.png 1.5x, /w/images/thumb/d/d6/Shoebox_models.png/600px-Shoebox_models.png 2x" data-file-width="1834" data-file-height="1114" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Shoebox_models.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Example Shoebox Models窶認enestration Analysis for a Typical Space</div></div></div>\n', '<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Detailed_models">Detailed models</span></h2>\n', '<p>Detailed models represent later stages of design. They are often used for refining or optimizing specific design strategies.\n', '</p>\n', '<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Compliance_models">Compliance models</span></h2>\n', '<p><a href="/wiki/Compliance_Models" title="Compliance Models">Compliance models</a> are another type of detailed model. of the model. \n', '</p><p>This page is coming soon and is planned to cover topics such as parametric analysis, scripting approaches to testing design alternatives, and automated data exchange between different software tools (such as BIM to BEM). Refer to the additional resources section below for links to external content.\n', '</p>\n', '<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Additional_Resources">Additional Resources</span></h2>\n', '<ul><li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=V_Ct_S1vtAs">BIM (Revit) to BEM Data Exchange</a> - This IBPSA-USA webinar (video) focuses on sharing best practices for developing BIM models so that they can effectively share data with BEM software tools.</li>\n', '<li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=lDN_nybJq20">Python Programming for Energy Modelers</a> - This IBPSA-USA webinar (video) focuses on outlining the process of acquiring data science skills for building performance analysts with little or no previous programming experience.</li>\n', '<li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://nrel.github.io/OpenStudio-user-documentation/getting_started/about_measures/">OpenStudio Measures</a> - In OpenStudio, a "Measure" is a set of programmatic instructions that makes changes to an energy model to reflect its application. A large library of these measures is available, or users can create their own. Measures can be applied to a specific model, or they can be more general for use across multiple models.</li>\n', '<li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://bigladdersoftware.com/projects/modelkit/">Modelkit</a> - Modelkit is a free and open-source, cross-platform framework for parametric modeling developed by Big Ladder Software. Modelkit integrates two powerful concepts: templates and scripting. Templates are an old method for combining static content with dynamic inputs. Scripting is a relatively new method for automating the process of modeling. Modelkit has been applied to EnergyPlus, the California Simulation Engine (CSE), and the California compliance software tools, CBECC-Com and CBECC-Res.</li>\n', '<li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://eppy.readthedocs.io/en/latest/readme.html">Eppy</a> - Eppy is a scripting language for EnergyPlus idf files, and EnergyPlus output files. Eppy is written in the programming language Python. It allows users to programmatically navigate, search, and modify EnergyPlus idf files.</li>\n', '<li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=IraNDbNcz3A">A Demo of Common BIM to BEM Workflows Using gbXML</a> - gbXML.org and IBPSA-USA sponsored this gbXML webinar. The webinar gives an overview of gbXML, a discussion about successes and struggles with BIM to BEM workflows using gbXML, and a presentation on the gbXML validator that was developed as part of an ASHRAE research project (RP-1810).</li>\n', '<li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://tools.zeroenvy.com/">BEM ToolBox</a> - The BEM ToolBox is a suite of tools used to parse model input and output files and present the data in a format that can be analyzed more effectively.  It is designed to automate repetitive tasks and  analyze model data, and the reports can be shared with other members of a project team.  The tools are geared towards users of IES-VE software although support for other software tools may be added.</li></ul>\n', '<p><small style="color: gray">Links to external websites are provided as a convenience for further research, but do not imply any endorsement of the content or the operator of the external site, as detailed in BEMcyclopedia\'s <a href="/wiki/Bemcyclopedia:General_disclaimer" title="Bemcyclopedia:General disclaimer">general disclaimers</a>.</small>\n', '</p>\n', '<!-- \n', 'NewPP limit report\n', 'Cached time: 20240320191705\n', 'Cache expiry: 86400\n', 'Dynamic content: false\n', 'Complications: []\n', 'CPU time usage: 0.006 seconds\n', 'Real time usage: 0.008 seconds\n', 'Preprocessor visited node count: 6/1000000\n', 'Post窶親xpand include size: 290/2097152 bytes\n', 'Template argument size: 0/2097152 bytes\n', 'Highest expansion depth: 2/40\n', 'Expensive parser function count: 0/100\n', 'Unstrip recursion depth: 0/20\n', 'Unstrip post窶親xpand size: 0/5000000 bytes\n', '-->\n', '<!--\n', 'Transclusion expansion time report (%,ms,calls,template)\n', '100.00%    1.181      1 Template:Additional_resources_disclaimer\n', '100.00%    1.181      1 -total\n', '-->\n', '\n', '<!-- Saved in parser cache with key bemcyclopedia_46-mw0f_:pcache:idhash:393-0!canonical and timestamp 20240320191705 and revision id 2102\n', ' -->\n', '</div><div id="bottom-notice-ns"><table cellspacing="5" cellpadding="0" style="margin: 0em 0em 1em 0em; border: 1px solid #1DA0E7; width: 100%">\n', '<tbody><tr>\n', '<td>Content is available under the <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://creativecommons.org/licenses/by-sa/3.0/">Creative Commons Attribution-ShareAlike License</a>; additional terms may apply. Policy</span></h2>\n', '<p>Last updated: December 15, 2021\n', '</p><p>This Privacy Policy describes Our policies and procedures on the collection, use and disclosure of Your information when You use the Service and tells You about Your privacy rights and how the law protects You.\n', '</p><p>We use Your Personal data to provide and improve the Service. By using the Service, You agree to the collection and use of information in accordance with this Privacy Policy. This Privacy Policy has been created with the help of the Privacy Policy Template.\n', '</p>\n', '<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Interpretation_and_Definitions">Interpretation and Definitions</span></h2>\n', '<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Interpretation">Interpretation</span></h3>\n', '<p>The words of which the initial letter is capitalized have meanings defined under the following conditions. The following definitions shall have the same meaning regardless of whether they appear in singular or in plural.\n', '</p>\n', '<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Definitions">Definitions</span></h3>\n', '<p>For the purposes of this Privacy Policy:\n', '</p>\n', '<ul><li><b>Account</b> means a unique account created for You to access our Service or parts of our Service.</li>\n', '<li><b>Company</b> (referred to as either "the Company", "We", "Us" or "Our" in this Agreement) refers to Model Efficiency, 35 Beharrell St #1093.</li>\n', '<li><b>Cookies</b> are small files that are placed on Your computer, mobile device or any other device by a website, containing the details of Your browsing history on that website among its many uses.</li>\n', '<li><b>Country</b> refers to: Massachusetts, United States</li>\n', '<li><b>Device</b> means any device that can access the Service such as a computer, a cellphone or a digital tablet.</li>\n', '<li><b>Personal Data</b> is any information that relates to an identified or identifiable individual.</li>\n', '<li><b>Service</b> refers to the Website.</li>\n', '<li><b>Service Provider</b> means any natural or legal person who processes the data on behalf of the Company. It refers to third-party companies or individuals employed by the Company to facilitate the Service, to provide the Service on behalf of the Company, to perform services related to the Service or to assist the Company in analyzing how the Service is used.</li>\n', '<li><b>Usage Data</b> refers to data collected automatically, either generated by the use of the Service or from the Service infrastructure itself (for example, the duration of a page visit).</li>\n', '<li><b>Website</b> refers to BEMcyclopedia, accessible from www.bemcyclopedia.com</li>\n', '<li><b>You</b> means the individual accessing or using the Service, or the company, or other legal entity on behalf of which such individual is accessing or using the Service, as applicable.</li></ul>\n', '<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Collecting_and_Using_Your_Personal_Data">Collecting and Using Your Personal Data</span></h2>\n', '<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Types_of_Data_Collected">Types of Data Collected</span></h3>\n', '<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_Data">Personal Data</span></h4>\n', '<p>While using Our Service, We may ask You to provide Us with certain personally identifiable information that can be used to contact or identify You. Personally identifiable information may include, but is not limited to:\n', '</p>\n', '<ul><li>Email address</li>\n', '<li>First name and last name</li>\n', '<li>Usage Data</li></ul>\n', '<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Usage_Data">Usage Data</span></h4>\n', '<p>Usage Data is collected automatically when using the Service.\n', "</p><p>Usage Data may include information such as Your Device's Internet Protocol address (e.g. IP address), browser type, browser version, the pages of our Service that You visit, the time and date of Your visit, the time spent on those pages, unique device identifiers and other diagnostic data.\n", '</p><p>When You access the Service by or through a mobile device, We may collect certain information automatically, including, but not limited to, the type of mobile device You use, Your mobile device unique ID, the IP address of Your mobile device, Your mobile operating system, the type of mobile Internet browser You use, unique device identifiers and other diagnostic data.\n', '</p><p>We may also collect information that Your browser sends whenever You visit our Service or when You access the Service by or through a mobile device.\n', '</p>\n', '<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Tracking_Technologies_and_Cookies">Tracking Technologies and Cookies</span></h4>\n', '<p>We use Cookies and similar tracking technologies to track the activity on Our Service and store certain information. Tracking technologies used are beacons, tags, and scripts to collect and track information and to improve and analyze Our Service. The technologies We use may include:\n', '</p>\n', '<ul><li><b>Cookies or Browser Cookies.</b> A cookie is a small file placed on Your Device. You can instruct Your browser to refuse all Cookies or to indicate when a Cookie is being sent. However, if You do not accept Cookies, You may not be able to use some parts of our Service. Unless you have adjusted Your browser setting so that it will refuse Cookies, our Service may use Cookies.</li>\n', '<li><b>Flash Cookies.</b> Certain features of our Service may use local stored objects (or Flash Cookies) to collect and store information about Your preferences or Your activity on our Service. Flash Cookies are not managed by the same browser settings as those used for Browser Cookies. For more information on how You can delete Flash Cookies, please read "Where can I change the settings for disabling, or deleting local shared objects?" available at https://helpx.adobe.com/flash-player/kb/disable-local-shared-objects-flash.html#main_Where_can_I_change_the_settings_for_disabling__or_deleting_local_shared_objects_</li>\n', '<li><b>Web Beacons.</b> Certain sections of our Service and our emails may contain small electronic files known as web beacons (also referred to as clear gifs, pixel tags, and single-pixel gifs) that permit the Company, for example, to count users who have visited those pages or opened an email and for other related website statistics (for example, recording the popularity of a certain section and verifying system and server integrity).</li></ul>\n', '<p>Cookies can be "Persistent" or "Session" Cookies. Persistent Cookies remain on Your personal computer or mobile device when You go offline, while Session Cookies are deleted as soon as You close Your web browser. You can learn more about cookies here: Cookies by TermsFeed Generator.\n', '</p><p>We use both Session and Persistent Cookies for the purposes set out below:\n', '</p>\n', '<ul><li><b>Necessary / Essential Cookies</b>  Type: Session Cookies  Administered by: Us  Purpose: These Cookies are essential to provide You with services available through the Website and to enable You to use some of its features. They help to authenticate users and prevent fraudulent use of user accounts. Without these Cookies, the services that You have asked for cannot be provided, and We only use these Cookies to provide You with those services.</li>\n', '<li><b>Cookies Policy / Notice Acceptance Cookies</b>  Type: Persistent Cookies  Administered by: Us  Purpose: These Cookies identify if users have accepted the use of cookies on the Website.</li>\n', '<li><b>Functionality Cookies</b>  Type: Persistent Cookies  Administered by: Us  Purpose: These Cookies allow us to remember choices You make when You use the Website, such as remembering your login details or language preference. The purpose of these Cookies is to provide You with a more personal experience and to avoid You having to re-enter your preferences every time You use the Website.</li></ul>\n', '<p>For more information about the cookies we use and your choices regarding cookies, please visit our Cookies Policy or the Cookies section of our Privacy Policy.\n', '</p>\n', '<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Use_of_Your_Personal_Data">Use of Your Personal Data</span></h3>\n', '<p>The Company may use Personal Data for the following purposes:\n', '</p>\n', '<ul><li><b>To provide and maintain our Service</b>, including to monitor the usage of our Service.</li>\n', '<li><b>To manage Your Account:</b> to manage Your registration as a user of the Service. The Personal Data You provide can give You access to different functionalities of the Service that are available to You as a registered user.</li>\n', '<li><b>For the performance of a contract:</b> the development, compliance and undertaking of the purchase contract for the products, items or services You have purchased or of any other contract with Us through the Service.</li>\n', "<li><b>To contact You:</b> To contact You by email, telephone calls, SMS, or other equivalent forms of electronic communication, such as a mobile application's push notifications regarding updates or informative communications related to the functionalities, products or contracted services, including the security updates, when necessary or reasonable for their implementation.</li>\n", '<li><b>To provide You</b> with news, special offers and general information about other goods, services and events which we offer that are similar to those that you have already purchased or enquired about unless You have opted not to receive such information.</li>\n', '<li><b>To manage Your requests:</b> To attend and manage Your requests to Us.</li>\n', '<li><b>For business transfers:</b> We may use Your information to evaluate or conduct a merger, divestiture, restructuring, reorganization, dissolution, or other sale or transfer of some or all of Our assets, whether as a going concern or as part of bankruptcy, liquidation, or similar proceeding, in which Personal Data held by Us about our Service users is among the assets transferred.</li>\n', '<li><b>For other purposes</b>: We may use Your information for other purposes, such as data analysis, identifying usage trends, determining the effectiveness of our promotional campaigns and to evaluate and improve our Service, products, services, marketing and your experience.</li></ul>\n', '<p>We may share Your personal information in the following situations:\n', '</p>\n', '<ul><li><b>With Service Providers:</b> We may share Your personal information with Service Providers to monitor and analyze the use of our Service, to contact You.</li>\n', '<li><b>For business transfers:</b> We may share or transfer Your personal information in connection with, or during negotiations of, any merger, sale of Company assets, financing, or acquisition of all or a portion of Our business to another company.</li>\n', '<li><b>With Affiliates:</b> We may share Your information with Our affiliates, in which case we will require those affiliates to honor this Privacy Policy. Affiliates include Our parent company and any other subsidiaries, joint venture partners or other companies that We control or that are under common control with Us.</li>\n', '<li><b>With business partners:</b> We may share Your information with Our business partners to offer You certain products, services or promotions.</li>\n', '<li><b>With other users:</b> when You share personal information or otherwise interact in the public areas with other users, such information may be viewed by all users and may be publicly distributed outside.</li>\n', '<li><b>With Your consent</b>: We may disclose Your personal information for any other purpose with Your consent.</li></ul>\n', '<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Retention_of_Your_Personal_Data">Retention of Your Personal Data</span></h3>\n', '<p>The Company will retain Your Personal Data only for as long as is necessary for the purposes set out in this Privacy Policy. We will retain and use Your Personal Data to the extent necessary to comply with our legal obligations (for example, if we are required to retain your data to comply with applicable laws), resolve disputes, and enforce our legal agreements and policies.\n', '</p><p>The Company will also retain Usage Data for internal analysis purposes. Usage Data is generally retained for a shorter period of time, except when this data is used to strengthen the security or to improve the functionality of Our Service, or We are legally obligated to retain this data for longer time periods.\n', '</p>\n', '<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Transfer_of_Your_Personal_Data">Transfer of Your Personal Data</span></h3>\n', "<p>Your information, including Personal Data, is processed at the Company's operating offices and in any other places where the parties involved in the processing are located. It means that this information may be transferred to 窶 and maintained on 窶 computers located outside of Your state, province, country or other governmental jurisdiction where the data protection laws may differ than those from Your jurisdiction.\n", '</p><p>Your consent to this Privacy Policy followed by Your submission of such information represents Your agreement to that transfer.\n', '</p><p>The Company will take all steps reasonably necessary to ensure that Your data is treated securely and in accordance with this Privacy Policy and no transfer of Your Personal Data will take place to an organization or a country unless there are adequate controls in place including the security of Your data and other personal information.\n', '</p>\n', '<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Disclosure_of_Your_Personal_Data">Disclosure of Your Personal Data</span></h3>\n', '<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Business_Transactions">Business Transactions</span></h4>\n', '<p>If the Company is involved in a merger, acquisition or asset sale, Your Personal Data may be transferred. We will provide notice before Your Personal Data is transferred and becomes subject to a different Privacy Policy.\n', '</p>\n', '<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Law_enforcement">Law enforcement</span></h4>\n', '<p>Under certain circumstances, the Company may be required to disclose Your Personal Data if required to do so by law or in response to valid requests by public authorities (e.g. a court or a government agency).\n', '</p>\n', '<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_legal_requirements">Other legal requirements</span></h4>\n', '<p>The Company may disclose Your Personal Data in the good faith belief that such action is necessary to:\n', '</p>\n', '<ul><li>Comply with a legal obligation</li>\n', '<li>Protect and defend the rights or property of the Company</li>\n', '<li>Prevent or investigate possible wrongdoing in connection with the Service</li>\n', '<li>Protect the personal safety of Users of the Service or the public</li>\n', '<li>Protect against legal liability</li></ul>\n', '<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Security_of_Your_Personal_Data">Security of Your Personal Data</span></h3>\n', '<p>The security of Your Personal Data is important to Us, but remember that no method of transmission over the Internet, or method of electronic storage is 100% secure. While We strive to use commercially acceptable means to protect Your Personal Data, We cannot guarantee its absolute security.\n', '</p>\n', '<h2><span id="Children\'s_Privacy"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Children.27s_Privacy">Children\'s Privacy</span></h2>\n', '<p>Our Service does not address anyone under the age of 13. We do not knowingly collect personally identifiable information from anyone under the age of 13. If You are a parent or guardian and You are aware that Your child has provided Us with Personal Data, please contact Us. If We become aware that We have collected Personal Data from anyone under the age of 13 without verification of parental consent, We take steps to remove that information from Our servers.\n', "</p><p>If We need to rely on consent as a legal basis for processing Your information and Your country requires consent from a parent, We may require Your parent's consent before We collect and use that information.\n", '</p>\n', '<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Links_to_Other_Websites">Links to Other Websites</span></h2>\n', "<p>Our Service may contain links to other websites that are not operated by Us. If You click on a third party link, You will be directed to that third party's site. We strongly advise You to review the Privacy Policy of every site You visit.\n", '</p><p>We have no control over and assume no responsibility for the content, privacy policies or practices of any third party sites or services.\n', '</p>\n', '<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Changes_to_this_Privacy_Policy">Changes to this Privacy Policy</span></h2>\n', '<p>We may update Our Privacy Policy from time to time. We will notify You of any changes by posting the new Privacy Policy on this page.\n', '</p><p>We will let You know via email and/or a prominent notice on Our Service, prior to the change becoming effective and update the "Last updated" date at the top of this Privacy Policy.\n', '</p><p>You are advised to review this Privacy Policy periodically for any changes. '\t<a id="top"></a>\n', '\t<div id="siteNotice" class="mw-body-content"></div>\n', '\t<div class="mw-indicators mw-body-content">\n', '\t</div>\n', '\t<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">Schematic Design</h1>\n', '\t<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">\n', '\t\t<div id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Bemcyclopedia</div>\n', '\t\t<div id="contentSub"><span class="subpages"><div id="breadcrumbs2"><a href="/wiki/BEMcyclopedia_-_The_Energy_Modeling_Knowledgebase" title="BEMcyclopedia - The Energy Modeling Knowledgebase">BEMcyclopedia</a> &gt; <a href="/wiki/Learn_by_Design_Task" title="Learn by Design Task">Learn by Design Task</a> &gt; <span id="breadcrumbs2-currentitle">Schematic Design</span></div></span></div>\n', '\t\t<div id="contentSub2"></div>\n', '\t\t\n', '\t\t<div id="jump-to-nav"></div>\n', '\t\t<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a>\n', '\t\t<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#searchInput">Jump to search</a>\n', '\t\t<div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><div class="mw-parser-output"><p>During the <b>schematic design</b> phase of a project, the project team will develop rough construction drawings that offer an overview of a project\'s features. While the level of detail is much less than the later stages of design, it is enough to generate construction cost estimates and allow the team to ensure that the design concepts fit within the project budget.<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup>\n', '</p><p>During this phase, the team will typically consider many design options and the decisions they make will inform the later stages of design.  This process of selecting different design options and concepts has a good amount of overlap with activities described in the <a href="/wiki/Conceptual_Design" title="Conceptual Design">conceptual design</a> section of this site. In fact, many projects will effectively merge the conceptual and schematic phases together and refer to this combined process as "schematic design."\n', '</p><p>The schematic design documents developed by the team include architectural floor plans and elevation drawings, as well as engineering plans for the HVAC, electrical and plumbing systems.  The architectural drawings will convey the basic layout of the building, and the engineering drawings will include system capacities and approximate locations.  Detailed aspects of the design are generally not included until the <a href="/wiki/Design_Development" title="Design Development">design development</a> phase.\n', '</p><p>BEM practitioners can be highly impactful during this phase by helping to analyze the energy and comfort impacts of each of the design options being considered by the team.  Read on for more guidance on BEM analysis that can inform the major architectural and engineering decisions made during schematic design.\n', '</p>\n', '<div id="toc" class="toc" role="navigation" aria-labelledby="mw-toc-heading"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" /><div class="toctitle" lang="en" dir="ltr"><h2 id="mw-toc-heading">Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label class="toctogglelabel" for="toctogglecheckbox"></label></span></div>\n', '<ul>\n', '<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-1"><a href="#Architectural_design_activities"><span class="tocnumber">1</span> <span class="toctext">Architectural design activities</span></a>\n', '<ul>\n', '<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-2"><a href="#Progression_of_main_design_concepts"><span class="tocnumber">1.1</span> <span class="toctext">Progression of main design concepts</span></a></li>\n', '<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-3"><a href="#Develop_preliminary_floor_plans"><span class="tocnumber">1.2</span> <span class="toctext">Develop preliminary floor plans</span></a></li>\n', '<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-4"><a href="#Develop_preliminary_facade_design_and_elevation_drawings"><span class="tocnumber">1.3</span> <span class="toctext">Develop preliminary facade design and elevation drawings</span></a></li>\n', '</ul>\n', '</li>\n', '<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-5"><a href="#Engineering_design_activities"><span class="tocnumber">2</span> <span class="toctext">Engineering design activities</span></a>\n', '<ul>\n', '<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-6"><a href="#Loads_analysis"><span class="tocnumber">2.1</span> <span class="toctext">Loads analysis</span></a></li>\n', '<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-7"><a href="#System_selection"><span class="tocnumber">2.2</span> <span class="toctext">System selection</span></a>\n', '<ul>\n', '<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-8"><a href="#HVAC_systems_selection"><span class="tocnumber">2.2.1</span> <span class="toctext">HVAC systems selection</span></a></li>\n', '<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-9"><a href="#Lighting_systems_selection"><span class="tocnumber">2.2.2</span> <span class="toctext">Lighting systems selection</span></a></li>\n', '</ul>\n', '</li>\n', '<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-10"><a href="#Develop_schematic_design_drawings"><span class="tocnumber">2.3</span> <span class="toctext">Develop schematic design drawings</span></a></li>\n', '<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-11"><a href="#Energy_.28and_other_metrics.29_estimation"><span class="tocnumber">2.4</span> <span class="toctext">Energy (and other metrics) estimation</span></a></li>\n', '</ul>\n', '</li>\n', '<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-12"><a href="#Integrated_design_strategies"><span class="tocnumber">3</span> <span class="toctext">Integrated design strategies</span></a>\n', '<ul>\n', '<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-13"><a href="#Thermal_comfort_strategy"><span class="tocnumber">3.1</span> <span class="toctext">Thermal comfort strategy</span></a></li>\n', '<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-14"><a href="#Indoor_air_quality_strategy"><span class="tocnumber">3.2</span> <span class="toctext">Indoor air quality strategy</span></a></li>\n', '<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-15"><a href="#Thermal_load_control_strategy"><span class="tocnumber">3.3</span> <span class="toctext">Thermal load control strategy</span></a></li>\n', '<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-16"><a href="#Daylighting_and_visual_comfort_strategy"><span class="tocnumber">3.4</span> <span class="toctext">Daylighting and visual comfort strategy</span></a></li>\n', '</ul>\n', '</li>\n', '<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-17"><a href="#Relevant_ASHRAE_Standard_209_cycles"><span class="tocnumber">4</span> <span class="toctext">Relevant ASHRAE Standard 209 cycles</span></a></li>\n', '<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-18"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">5</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a></li>\n', '</ul>\n', '</div>\n', '\n', '<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Architectural_design_activities">Architectural design activities</span></h2>\n', "<p>During the schematic design phase, the architects begin to integrate the project's space needs and design goals into a set of floor plans. This is a highly iterative process where much coordination occurs between the architect and the building owner. Often, several options are presented to the building owner showing different designs and space layout, and the owner's feedback is used to refine the design.  In addition to floor plan drawings, this information may also be presented in other formats such as 3D renderings or models.\n", "</p><p>Many of the key design decisions are made during this stage. Decisions about the building's form and elevation/facade design can have large impacts on the building's performance and BEM analysis can be very informative in the decision making process.\n", '</p>\n', '<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Progression_of_main_design_concepts">Progression of main design concepts</span></h3>\n', '<p>During this phase, the design concepts that were identified during the <a href="/wiki/Conceptual_Design#Design_Features" title="Conceptual Design">conceptual design phase</a> will continue to be explored, vetted, and selected for inclusion in the building design. BEM analysis can support the architectural team by evaluating:\n', '</p>\n', '<ul><li><b><a href="/wiki/Constructions_and_thermal_mass_options" title="Constructions and thermal mass options">Constructions and thermal mass options</a></b></li>\n', '<li><b><a href="/wiki/Fenestration_and_daylighting_options" title="Fenestration and daylighting options">Fenestration and daylighting options</a></b></li>\n', '<li><b><a href="/wiki/Natural_ventilation_design_features" title="Natural ventilation design features">Natural ventilation design features</a></b></li>\n', '<li><b><a href="/wiki/Passive_solar_design_features" title="Passive solar design features">Passive solar design features</a></b></li></ul>\n', '<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Develop_preliminary_floor_plans">Develop preliminary floor plans</span></h3>\n', '<p>A primary goal of the schematic design phase is to develop floor plan drawings that include the space type needs for the building as defined when creating the <a href="/wiki/Pre-Design#Building_Program" title="Pre-Design">building program</a>. The physical locations of the various space types are designed for functionality, flow, occupants\' experience, and many other factors.\n', '</p><p>The BEM practitioner, or mechanical engineer, will ultimately use the floor plan layout as the basis for performing load calculations and early-stage energy modeling. Because the schematic design phase considers many options, the BEM analysis can provide feedback on how each option performs relative to one another. Helpful modeling tasks may include:\n', '</p>\n', '<ul><li><b><a href="/wiki/Analysis_of_energy_and_comfort_impacts_of_different_programming_layouts" title="Analysis of energy and comfort impacts of different programming layouts">Analysis of energy and comfort impacts of different programming layouts</a></b></li>\n', '<li><b><a href="/wiki/Analysis_of_the_impact_of_locations_of_special_zones" title="Analysis of the impact of locations of special zones">Analysis of the impact of locations of special zones</a></b> such as conference rooms, equipment rooms, and others</li>\n', '<li><b><a href="/wiki/Analysis_of_how_HVAC_loads_differ_for_different_programming_layouts" title="Analysis of how HVAC loads differ for different programming layouts">Analysis of how HVAC loads differ for different programming layouts</a></b> and how this may impact architectural needs such as shaft sizes, equipment room sizes, and plenum heights</li></ul>\n', '<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Develop_preliminary_facade_design_and_elevation_drawings">Develop preliminary facade design and elevation drawings</span></h3>\n', "<p>The elevation drawings show the building's facade design and call out construction material types, window sizes and locations, locations of other openings such as doors and louvers, shading, and other features.  \n", "</p><p>The facade is an essential element that defines the building's character, provides protection from the elements, and contributes to its energy efficiency.  BEM analysis can contribute to the facade design process in a number of ways:\n", '</p>\n', '<ul><li><b>Window-to-wall ratio parametric studies</b> to determine performance impacts of different window areas including solar gains and daylighting potential</li>\n', '<li><b>Shading feature design analysis</b></li>\n', '<li><b>Analysis of potential for natural ventilation and passive cooling</b> with operable windows</li>\n', '<li><b>Analysis of thermal performance of different wall construction materials</b></li>\n', '<li><b>Analysis of thermal performance of different glazing performance specifications</b></li></ul>\n', '<p>The BEM studies may analyze whole-building performance using a <a href="/wiki/Simple_Box_Models" title="Simple Box Models">simple box model</a>, or they may be focused studies on a specific building orientation or room type using <a href="/wiki/Shoebox_Models" title="Shoebox Models">shoebox models</a>.\n', '</p>\n', '<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Engineering_design_activities">Engineering design activities</span></h2>\n', '<p>The engineering team collaborates closely with the architects to ensure that the building systems meet the functional needs of the building.  The mechanical (HVAC) engineers consider aspects such as indoor air quality and comfort; the electrical engineers consider power and lighting needs. System selections often consider the tradeoffs between equipment cost and energy efficiency (operational costs), and also how the system choice may impact compliance with the energy code.  \n', '</p><p>HVAC system energy will account for a significant proportion of a building\'s total energy use.  The amount will vary depending on the architectural design (e.g. <a href="/wiki/Compare_Massing_Options" title="Compare Massing Options">massing</a> and facade design), the planned usage of the building and the amount of <a href="/wiki/Basics_of_internal_gains" title="Basics of internal gains">internal gains</a>. Energy analysis is crucial at this stage to ensure that the performance of building systems is considered in the design.\n', '</p>\n', '<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Loads_analysis">Loads analysis</span></h3>\n', '<p>HVAC load calculation analysis is a process to determine the heating, ventilation, and air conditioning requirements for each space and system within the building. Loads analysis helps the HVAC engineers design all aspects of the system including system sizes (heating and cooling capacity), flow rates for air and water, ductwork and diffuser sizes, etc. However, during schematic design, the goal is not to design every element of the system yet.  Schematic design load analysis focuses on determining overall heating and cooling capacities so that approximate sizes for boilers, chillers, and air handling systems can be identified (and included in cost estimation processes). This big-picture sizing information is also used to coordinate with the architects so that they can allocate sufficient space for equipment rooms, mechanical shafts (to route large ducts vertically between floors), and ceiling plenum cavities (to run ducts and other system features above the ceilings).\n', '</p><p>Loads analysis is similar in many ways to whole-building BEM except that, where BEM analysis focuses on calculating performance <u>over a period of time</u> (e.g. an annual analysis), loads analysis is focused just on calculating performance at <u>peak conditions</u> (e.g. the hottest and coldest days of the year). \n', '</p><p>Loads analysis is often performed by the HVAC engineering team, often by a member of the team who also performs BEM analysis.  Often the BEM practitioner (whether they are part of the HVAC design team, or an external consultant) will be consulted at this stage to identify ways to reduce the loads in the building.  Reducing the loads can result in smaller system capacities (saving first costs, reducing the size of equipment rooms, vertical shafts, and plenum height), improved thermal comfort, and significant operational energy cost savings.\n', '</p>\n', '<ul><li><b>Load reduction modeling</b></li></ul>\n', '<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="System_selection">System selection</span></h3>\n', '<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="HVAC_systems_selection">HVAC systems selection</span></h4>\n', '<p>The choice of HVAC system may be based on many factors:\n', '</p>\n', '<ul><li>Efficiency - some system types are inherently more efficient than others. Projects that have set <a href="/wiki/Set_performance_goals_for_the_project" title="Set performance goals for the project">performance goals</a> may be more likely to evaluate a range of low-energy system types.</li>\n', '<li>Cost - system costs may vary based on their complexity to manufacture and to install. An analysis of first costs vs. ongoing operational costs (e.g. payback analysis or life cycle cost analysis) is important to understand the true cost implications of selecting a system type.</li>\n', '<li>Expertise - some design firms may have more experience with a certain system type and therefore may be likely to select that system over an alternative type.</li>\n', '<li>Capacity - some system types have the ability to provide more cooling or heating per square foot of area than others. It is important to understand the amount of loads in each space and ensure that the system can meet the load density (load per square foot).</li></ul>\n', '<p>BEM analysis that can help to inform the system selection:\n', '</p>\n', '<ul><li><b><a href="/wiki/Compare_the_performance_of_different_HVAC_system_options" title="Compare the performance of different HVAC system options">Compare the performance of different HVAC system options</a></b></li></ul>\n', '<p>Read more about different HVAC system type options: <a href="/wiki/HVAC_system_types" title="HVAC system types"><b>HVAC system types</b></a>\n', '</p>\n', '<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Lighting_systems_selection">Lighting systems selection</span></h4>\n', '<p>During schematic design, the lighting system design will focus on analyzing the building space types, determining desired illuminance levels, selecting lighting fixture types, and selecting desired control options for the lights. \n', '</p><p>BEM analysis that can inform the lighting system design:\n', '</p>\n', '<ul><li><b><a href="/wiki/Test_strategies_to_reduce_lighting_power_density" title="Test strategies to reduce lighting power density">Test strategies to reduce lighting power density</a></b> and quantifying energy impacts</li>\n', '<li><b><a href="/wiki/Analyze_the_impact_of_lighting_control_strategies" title="Analyze the impact of lighting control strategies">Analyze the impact of lighting control strategies</a></b> such as occupant sensor and daylight sensor controls</li></ul>\n', '<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Develop_schematic_design_drawings">Develop schematic design drawings</span></h3>\n', '<p>The schematic design drawings and supporting documentation are at a high level, but with sufficient detail to begin estimating the construction costs. \n', '</p><p>HVAC drawings include approximate sizes and locations for major equipment such as chillers, boilers, cooling towers, and air handling units. Major duct runs are typically depicted as single lines, but with the duct dimensions called out.  Vertical ductwork (through shafts) are generally drawn in 2D to demonstrate they will fit within the architectural shaft spaces.  The HVAC specifications and other supporting documents will indicate the basis of design and include information such as design set point temperatures, assumptions of thermal properties of the building envelope used for load calculations, description of any special features of the system including planned control strategies.\n', '</p><p>BEM analysis is not typically a key component when drafting the design documents, however the load calculation process and system selection analysis that precedes the drawing phase is of utmost importance to selecting appropriate system types and ensuring the accuracy of the system sizes shown on the drawings.\n', '</p>\n', '<h3><span id="Energy_(and_other_metrics)_estimation"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Energy_.28and_other_metrics.29_estimation">Energy (and other metrics) estimation</span></h3>\n', '<p>During the schematic design phase, many fundamental design decisions are made that will have significant impacts on the performance of the building. As the design progresses to later stages (design development and construction documents), it becomes increasingly difficult to change these early decisions without significant and costly redesign.  Therefore, it is important that the energy and other performance metrics be estimated during schematic design to understand how the building performs relative to specific <a href="/wiki/Set_performance_goals_for_the_project" title="Set performance goals for the project">project performance goals</a>, <a href="/wiki/Determine_the_applicable_energy_code" title="Determine the applicable energy code">code compliance</a>, or <a href="/wiki/Determine_applicability_of_beyond-code_programs" title="Determine applicability of beyond-code programs">beyond-code program</a> performance. If BEM analysis shows the project is not meeting the performance goals or complying with the code, changes can be made rather easily at this stage.   \n', '</p><p>A typical approach during SD is to use <a href="/wiki/Simple_Box_Models" title="Simple Box Models">simple box models</a> to capture a baseline performance (often a code-minimum baseline), and then test various design strategies against the baseline to determine how each measure, or combinations of multiple measures impacts the performance. \n', '</p>\n', '<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Integrated_design_strategies">Integrated design strategies</span></h2>\n', '<p>Many design decisions affect both the architectural and engineering designs, especially for high-performance buildings. It is important for the architectural and engineering teams to coordinate when developing big-picture strategies and continuing this collaboration as the strategies are developed.  \n', '</p>\n', '<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Thermal_comfort_strategy">Thermal comfort strategy</span></h3>\n', '<p>Design concepts to explore include:\n', '</p>\n', '<ul><li>Natural ventilation</li>\n', '<li>Ceiling fans</li>\n', '<li>Mechanical cooling</li>\n', '<li>Radiant systems</li>\n', '<li>Occupant control</li></ul>\n', '<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Indoor_air_quality_strategy">Indoor air quality strategy</span></h3>\n', '<p>Design concepts to explore include:\n', '</p>\n', '<ul><li>Mechanical ventilation</li>\n', '<li>Natural ventilation</li>\n', '<li>Filtration</li>\n', '<li>Source control</li>\n', '<li>Demand control ventilation</li></ul>\n', '<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Thermal_load_control_strategy">Thermal load control strategy</span></h3>\n', '<p>Design concepts to explore include:\n', '</p>\n', '<ul><li>Exterior shading</li>\n', '<li>Interior shading</li>\n', '<li>Glazing selection and area</li>\n', '<li>Insulation</li>\n', '<li>Cool roof</li>\n', '<li>Thermal mass</li></ul>\n', '<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Daylighting_and_visual_comfort_strategy">Daylighting and visual comfort strategy</span></h3>\n', '<p>Design concepts to explore include:\n', '</p>\n', '<ul><li>Daylight</li>\n', '<li>Electric lighting</li>\n', '<li>Shading devices</li>\n', '<li>Task lighting vs. ambient lighting</li>\n', '<li>Narrow building</li>\n', '<li>Top lighting</li>\n', '<li>Side lighting</li></ul>\n', '<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Relevant_ASHRAE_Standard_209_cycles">Relevant ASHRAE Standard 209 cycles</span></h2>\n', '<p>Several <a href="/wiki/ASHRAE_Standard_209-2018" title="ASHRAE Standard 209-2018">ASHRAE Standard 209</a> cycles are applicable to the schematic design phase, including:\n', '</p>\n', '<ul><li>Cycle 2 - Conceptual design modeling</li>\n', '<li>Cycle 3 - Load reduction modeling</li>\n', '<li>Cycle 4 - HVAC system selection modeling</li></ul>\n', '<h2><span class="mw-headline" '<nav id="p-Essential BEM Concepts" class="vector-menu vector-menu-portal portal" aria-labelledby="p-Essential BEM Concepts-label" role="navigation" \n', '\t >\n', '\t<h3 id="p-Essential BEM class="mw-parser-output"><p>As an energy modeler, it is important to understand how various <b>codes and standards</b> apply to a building project. Codes describe <b>requirements</b> that must be met by projects and are enforced during the design and construction process. Standards may either represent 窶彙est practices窶 for design (and therefore are often followed), or, in many cases, they may be adopted by a code agency and therefore are required to be followed.\n', '</p><p>In addition to specifying design characteristics that must be met, codes and standards also offer a wealth of information that can be useful for energy modelers including many numerical values that can be directly used as inputs for the models, or values that can be used to perform quality assurance on the models.\n', '</p><p>This page describes several categories of codes and standards and their relevance to energy modeling.<span id="building-codes"></span>\n', '</p>\n', '<div id="toc" class="toc" role="navigation" aria-labelledby="mw-toc-heading"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" /><div class="toctitle" lang="en" dir="ltr"><h2 id="mw-toc-heading">Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label
