'</div>\n', '\n', '<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Building_codes">Building codes</span></h2>\n', '<p>The building code is a set of rules that specify how buildings must be constructed and the focus of the code is primarily to protect public health and safety for the construction and occupancy of the building. Buildings must comply with the code to obtain permits.<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup>\n', '</p><p>The scope of building codes include structural, egress, fire safety, construction materials requirements, occupancy rules, and design and construction requirements for the building systems such as mechanical, electrical, lighting, and plumbing. Energy efficiency codes and standards are also included as a building code requirement.\n', '</p>\n', '<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Energy_codes_and_standards">Energy codes and standards</span></h2>\n', '<p>Energy codes are a subset of the broader building code requirements. While building codes focus on ensuring safety, energy codes are designed to ensure that buildings are designed and built to meet a specified level of energy efficiency.<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup>\n', '</p><p>Energy codes may either be implemented following a prescriptive approach or a performance approach. The performance approach can be met by developing energy models to demonstrate that the proposed building design meets a specified energy budget, target, or other threshold. Different energy codes have different set of rules for creating the model and determining whether the modeled building passes or fails.  For additional guidance on understanding modeling rules of the performance approach, refer to the page <a href="/wiki/Determine_the_applicable_energy_code" title="Determine the applicable energy code">Determine the applicable energy code</a>. <span id="national-codes-model-energy-codes"></span>\n', '</p>\n', '<h3><span id="National_Codes_(Model_Energy_Codes)"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="National_Codes_.28Model_Energy_Codes.29">National Codes (Model Energy Codes)</span></h3>\n', '<ul><li>ASHRAE Standard 90.1</li>\n', '<li>IECC</li>\n', '<li>User窶冱 Manuals<span id="state-and-local-codes"></span><span id="state-and-local-codes"></span></li></ul>\n', '<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="State_and_Local_Codes">State and Local Codes</span></h3>\n', '<ul><li>Local jurisdictions will usually adopt the model codes with some amendments 窶 variations of the above with requirements that may be slightly different, usually to respond to local climate conditions. Some states develop their energy code independently from the model national codes</li>\n', '<li>Title 24</li>\n', '<li>Also, refer to the <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://bemcyclopedia.com/links.html#Codes%20and%20Standards">BEMcyclopedia Links Page</a> for additional i<span id="ventilation-codes-and-standards"></span>nformation about Codes and Standards.</li></ul>\n', '<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Energy_modeling_codes_and_standards">Energy modeling codes and standards</span></h2>\n', '<ul><li><a href="/wiki/ASHRAE_Standard_209-2018" title="ASHRAE Standard 209-2018">ASHRAE Standard 209</a> - "Energy Simulation Aided Design for Buildings" - Standard 209\'s purpose is to 窶廛efine minimum requirements for providing energy design assistance using building energy simulation and analysis窶<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup></li>\n', '<li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.energy.gov/eere/buildings/ashrae-standard-205-maintenance-and-development">ASHRAE Standard 205</a> -  "Standard Representation of Performance Simulation Data for HVAC&amp;R and Other Facility Equipment" defines performance maps for HVAC equipment from coils and fans to chillers and VRF systems. The Standard Project Committee works with manufacturers to develop and publish performance data sets and with BEM vendors to support the use of performance maps in BEM engines.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup></li>\n', '<li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.energy.gov/eere/buildings/ashrae-standard-140-maintenance-and-development">ASHRAE Standard 140</a> - 窶彜tandard Method of Test for Building Energy Simulation Computer Programs窶 aims to increase confidence in the use of building energy modeling (BEM) by creating standardized and citable test procedures for validating, diagnosing, and improving the current generation of BEM software.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> <span id="energy-codes-and-standards"></span><span id="ventilation-codes-and-standards"></span></li></ul>\n', '<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Ventilation_codes_and_standards">Ventilation codes and standards</span></h2>\n', '<p>ASHRAE Standard 62.1 specifies minimum ventilation rates and other measures intended to provide indoor air quality (IAQ) that窶冱 acceptable to human occupants and that minimizes adverse health effects. The standard provides procedures and methods for meeting minimum ventilation and IAQ requirements to engineers, design professionals, owners, and jurisdictional authorities where model codes have been adopted.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup>  For additional guidance on ventilation codes and standards, refer to the page <a href="/wiki/Determine_ventilation_requirements" title="Determine ventilation requirements">Determine ventilation requirements</a>. \n', '</p>\n', '<ul><li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.ashrae.org/technical-resources/bookstore/standards-62-1-62-2">ASHRAE Standard 62.1</a> - "Ventilation and Acceptable Indoor Air Quality"</li>\n', '<li>Local building codes - many adopt some vintage 62.1 requirements, but this is not universally true. If 62.1, be sure you know which version, and if not, consult the local code<span id="thermal-comfort-codes-and-standards"></span></li></ul>\n', '<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Thermal_comfort_codes_and_standards">Thermal comfort codes and standards</span></h2>\n', '<ul><li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" Each is useful for different types of model analysis, and collectively enable a thorough analysis of a building's performance.\n", '</p>\n', '<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Annual_output_results">Annual output results</span></h3>\n', '<p>Annual outputs for building energy models typically provide a comprehensive overview of yearly energy consumption, costs, and other performance metrics. \n', '</p>\n', '<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Monthly_output_results">Monthly output results</span></h3>\n', '<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Output_data_example-bar_and_pie_chart-consumption_by_end_use.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="/w/images/thumb/a/ab/Output_data_example-bar_and_pie_chart-consumption_by_end_use.png/300px-Output_data_example-bar_and_pie_chart-consumption_by_end_use.png" decoding="async" width="300" height="295" class="thumbimage" srcset="/w/images/thumb/a/ab/Output_data_example-bar_and_pie_chart-consumption_by_end_use.png/450px-Output_data_example-bar_and_pie_chart-consumption_by_end_use.png 1.5x, /w/images/thumb/a/ab/Output_data_example-bar_and_pie_chart-consumption_by_end_use.png/600px-Output_data_example-bar_and_pie_chart-consumption_by_end_use.png 2x" data-file-width="1052" data-file-height="1035" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Output_data_example-bar_and_pie_chart-consumption_by_end_use.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Pie chart and bar chart illustrating energy consumption by end use. (Source: IBPSA-USA BEM Workshop)</div></div></div>\n', '<p>Monthly outputs offer a more detailed breakdown, highlighting variations throughout the year. \n', '</p>\n', '<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Timestep_output_results">Timestep output results</span></h3>\n', '<p>Timestep outputs are reported at specific intervals, often hourly or even smaller. Analyzing these outputs offering a  view of energy usage and system behavior over time. Individual timestep results are useful for evaluating instantaneous loads, or system demand. \n', '</p>\n', '<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Granularity_of_output_results">Granularity of output results</span></h2>\n', '<p>Output results are also available at different levels of granularity. \n', '</p>\n', '<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Whole-building-level_outputs">Whole-building-level outputs</span></h3>\n', '<p>Whole-building outputs in energy models encapsulate overall performance metrics like total energy consumption, costs, and environmental impact. Whole-building-level outputs may be further broken down by fuel type (electricity vs. gas), or end use.\n', '</p>\n', '<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Zone-level_outputs">Zone-level outputs</span></h3>\n', '<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Output_data_example-week_timestep_plot-zone_temps.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="/w/images/thumb/a/ad/Output_data_example-week_timestep_plot-zone_temps.png/300px-Output_data_example-week_timestep_plot-zone_temps.png" decoding="async" width="300" height="162" class="thumbimage" srcset="/w/images/thumb/a/ad/Output_data_example-week_timestep_plot-zone_temps.png/450px-Output_data_example-week_timestep_plot-zone_temps.png 1.5x, /w/images/thumb/a/ad/Output_data_example-week_timestep_plot-zone_temps.png/600px-Output_data_example-week_timestep_plot-zone_temps.png 2x" data-file-width="1556" data-file-height="841" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Output_data_example-week_timestep_plot-zone_temps.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Line plot illustrating variation of zone temperatures over the course of the year (top image) and over the period of a week in the summer and winter (bottom images). (Source: IBPSA-USA BEM Workshop)</div></div></div>\n', '<p>Zone-level outputs focus on individual spaces within the building. These outputs may include space temperatures, comfort settings, or energy consumption of equipment within a particular space. \n', '</p>\n', '<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="System-level_outputs">System-level outputs</span></h3>\n', '<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Output_data_example-timestep_plot-coil_loads.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="/w/images/thumb/a/a1/Output_data_example-timestep_plot-coil_loads.png/300px-Output_data_example-timestep_plot-coil_loads.png" decoding="async" width="300" height="244" class="thumbimage" srcset="/w/images/thumb/a/a1/Output_data_example-timestep_plot-coil_loads.png/450px-Output_data_example-timestep_plot-coil_loads.png 1.5x, /w/images/thumb/a/a1/Output_data_example-timestep_plot-coil_loads.png/600px-Output_data_example-timestep_plot-coil_loads.png 2x" data-file-width="1179" data-file-height="960" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Output_data_example-timestep_plot-coil_loads.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Line plot illustrating variation in heating and cooling coil loads over the course of a year. (Source: IBPSA-USA BEM Workshop)</div></div></div>\n', "<p>System-level outputs analyze the performance of HVAC, lighting, or other building systems, offering a detailed understanding of each system's contribution to overall energy usage. \n", '</p>\n', '<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_levels_of_granularity">Other levels of granularity</span></h3>\n', '<p>Some BEM software tools allow for tracking performance using "meters" which allow you to group various items together. This can be useful for evaluating performance of a particular section of a building. One example may be to evaluate the performance individual residential units in a multifamily building.\n', '</p>\n', '<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Useful_metrics">Useful metrics</span></h2>\n', '<p>This section lists useful energy model outputs, and the following sections cover how to apply them to verify model quality and answer design questions. \n', '</p><p>Several outputs will be important for nearly every project:\n', '</p>\n', '<ul><li>Electricity and gas consumption by end use - annual and monthly</li>\n', '<li>Peak electric demand by end use - monthly</li>\n', '<li>Energy cost by source - annual</li>\n', '<li>Air handler peak cooling and heating demand - annual</li>\n', '<li>Chilled water and hot water loop peak loads</li>\n', '<li>Unmet heating and cooling load hours</li></ul>\n', '<p>These additional outputs can also be useful when checking the quality of the model as well as with providing insights into building performance: \n', '</p>\n', '<ul><li>Energy consumption by source - hourly or sub-hourly</li>\n', '<li>Air handler cooling and heating demand - hourly or sub-hourly</li>\n', '<li>Chilled water and hot water loop demand - hourly or sub-hourly</li>\n', '<li>Peak cooling and heating loads by component, e.g. walls, roof, window solar, etc.</li>\n', '<li>Air handler hourly data: supply air flow, outdoor air flow, supply air temperature, cooling coil load, heating coil load, fan power</li>\n', '<li>Chilled water and hot water loop hourly data: flow, load, supply temperature, return temperature</li>\n', '<li>Zone air temperature</li></ul>\n', '<p>Output reports that summarize inputs and equipment capacities are useful for verifying the model and are produced by some simulation programs: \n', '</p>\n', '<ul><li>A list of zones that summarizes load inputs such as lighting power, occupant density, plug load, and floor area</li>\n', '<li>A list of envelope components with performance values such as U-factor and SHGC.</li>\n', '<li>Description of air handlers including autosized airflow, cooling capacity and heating capacity as well as efficiency.</li>\n', '<li>Description of chilled water and hot water loops including autosized capacity and efficiency.</li></ul>\n', '<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Review_and_analysis_to_verify_model_quality">Review and analysis to verify model quality</span></h2>\n', '<p>Even a simple box model presents many opportunities for unintended inputs. An output review can help verify model quality and confirm that the model represents your intended inputs\n', '</p>\n', '<ul><li><b>Tutorial:</b> <a href="/wiki/Review_and_analysis_to_verify_model_quality" title="Review and analysis to verify model quality">Review and analysis to verify model quality</a></li></ul>\n', '<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Analysis_to_provide_answers_and_insights">Analysis to provide answers and insights</span></h2>\n', '<p>BEM can be extremely effective at providing guidance on design decisions throughout all phases of a project, and at developing strategies to meet performance targets.  An overview is provided below, but for much more detail and guidance on using BEM to inform specific design tasks, please visit the <a href="/wiki/Learn_by_Design_Task" title="Learn by Design Task">Learn by Design Task</a> section of this site.\n', '</p>\n', '<ul><li><b>Overview:</b> <a href="/wiki/Analysis_to_provide_answers_and_insights" title="Analysis to provide answers and insights">Analysis to provide answers and insights</a></li>\n', '<li><b>See also:</b>\n', '<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Learn_by_Design_Task" title="Learn by Design Task">Learn by Design Task</a></li>\n', '<li><a href="/wiki/Presenting_results_visually" title="Presenting results visually">Presenting results visually</a></li></ul></li></ul>\n', '<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Presenting_the_results">Presenting the results</span></h2>\n', '<p>Energy modeling results have little value if decision makers do not understand them. When presenting results to owners and design teams here are two recommendations. \n', '</p>\n', '<ul><li>Focus on answering design questions rather than presenting simulation results</li>\n', '<li>Present information visually</li></ul>\n', '<p>The overview below includes several examples of energy model results presented graphically but for much more detail and guidance on presenting results relevant to specific design tasks, please visit the <a href="/wiki/Learn_by_Design_Task" title="Learn by Design Task">Learn by Design Task</a> section of this site. \n', '</p>\n', '<ul><li><b>Overview:</b> <a href="/wiki/Presenting_results_visually" title="Presenting results visually">Presenting results visually</a></li>\n', '<li><b>Tutorial:</b> <a href="/wiki/Presenting_an_input_summary" title="Presenting an input summary">Presenting an input summary</a></li>\n', '<li><b>Overview:</b> <a href="/wiki/Types_of_charts" title="Types of charts">Types of charts</a></li>\n', '<li><b>See also:</b>\n', '<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Learn_by_Design_Task" title="Learn by Design Task">Learn by Design Task</a></li>\n', '<li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://projectstasio.com/">Project Stasio</a></li>\n', '<li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://content.aia.org/sites/default/files/2019-06/Energy_Design_Modeling_Guide_v4.pdf">Architect窶冱 Guide to Building Performance</a> (AIA)</li></ul></li></ul>\n', '<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Accuracy_and_Uncertainty">Accuracy and Uncertainty</span></h2>\n', '<p>Building energy simulation programs are quite accurate when we provide accurate inputs. That can be a challenge for many cases, especially for early design models when many assumptions are necessary.\n', '</p><p>Often, during the design process, the focus of BEM analysis is comparing alternative design options. The relative performance of different designs is less sensitive to those assumptions, assuming that assumptions are consistent between the alternative models.\n', '</p><p>However, if the goal is to calculate an estimate of absolute energy consumption, then precise inputs are very important, and if the inputs align with real-world design and operation, then models can produce very accurate results.\n', '</p><p>Read more about <a href="/wiki/Accuracy_and_Uncertainty" title="Accuracy and Uncertainty">Accuracy and Uncertainty</a>.\n', '</p>\n', '<!-- \n', 'NewPP limit report\n', 'Cached time: 20240320191707\n', 'Cache expiry: 86400\n', 'Dynamic content: false\n', 'Complications: []\n', 'CPU time usage: 0.021 seconds\n', 'Real time usage: 0.025 seconds\n', 'Preprocessor visited node count: 69/1000000\n', 'Post窶親xpand include size: 132/2097152 bytes\n', 'Template argument size: 0/2097152 bytes\n', 'Highest expansion depth: 2/40\n', 'Expensive parser function count: 0/100\n', 'Unstrip recursion depth: 0/20\n', 'Unstrip post窶親xpand size: 0/5000000 bytes\n', '-->\n', '<!--\n', 'Transclusion expansion time report (%,ms,calls,template)\n', '100.00%    1.434      1 -total\n', ' 82.36%    1.181      4 Template:IBPSA_source\n', '-->\n', '\n', '<!-- Saved in parser cache with key bemcyclopedia_46-mw0f_:pcache:idhash:373-0!canonical and timestamp 20240320191707 and revision id 2469\n', ' -->\n', '</div><div id="bottom-notice-ns"><table cellspacing="5" cellpadding="0" style="margin: 0em 0em 1em 0em; border: 1px solid #1DA0E7; width: 100%">\n', '<tbody><tr>\n', '<td>Content is available under the <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://creativecommons.org/licenses/by-sa/3.0/">Creative Commons Attribution-ShareAlike License</a>; additional terms may apply. class="noprint">From Bemcyclopedia</div>\n', '\t\t<div id="contentSub"><span class="subpages"><div id="breadcrumbs2"><span id="breadcrumbs2-currentitle">BEMcyclopedia - The Energy Modeling navigation</a>\n', '\t\t<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#searchInput">Jump to search</a>\n', '\t\t<div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><div class="mw-parser-output"><p>BEMcyclopedia was created as a <b>free resource for energy modelers</b> to learn about building energy modeling (BEM), and to share their knowledge with others. The content is organized into two main areas. The "Learn by Design Task" section of the site is a collection of educational resources, organized around a typical building design project窶冱 timeline.&#160; The "Essential BEM Concepts" section is a collection of general BEM knowledge and fundamental skills that apply to a variety of BEM tasks. \n', '</p><p>The scope of this site is focused on building performance analysis with a focus on energy and emissions.  Other building analysis types such as daylight analysis and CFD are not explicitly covered, except where they may be integral to a specific type of energy analysis. All content is intended to be described in a "software-neutral" manner such that the guidance may be applied to any energy modeling software that you may choose to use.  \n', '</p><p>Anyone can contribute! This site\'s content is provided for the BEM community, by the BEM community.  <b><a href="/wiki/Special:CreateAccount" title="Special:CreateAccount">Create an account</a></b> today to get started!  Then, learn more about how the site is organized, how to contribute, how to get editing rights, and guidelines for contributions by visiting the <a href="/wiki/Help_Guide_for_Contributing_to_BEMcyclopedia" title="Help Guide for Contributing to BEMcyclopedia"><b>help guide for contributors</b></a>.\n', '</p><p><br />\n', '</p>\n', '<table class="wikitable" style="width: 95%; margin: auto;">\n', '\n', '<tbody><tr>\n', '<th style="width: 50%"><big> <a href="/wiki/Learn_by_Design_Task" title="Learn by Design Task">Learn by Design Task</a> </big>\n', '</th>\n', '<th style="width: 50%"><big> <a href="/wiki/Essential_Concepts" title="Essential Concepts">Essential BEM Concepts</a>\n', '</big></th></tr>\n', '<tr style="vertical-align:top;">\n', '<td style="padding: 20px"><div class="center"><div class="floatnone"><img alt="001-blueprint.png" src="/w/images/thumb/0/00/001-blueprint.png/128px-001-blueprint.png" decoding="async" width="128" height="128" srcset="/w/images/thumb/0/00/001-blueprint.png/192px-001-blueprint.png 1.5x, /w/images/thumb/0/00/001-blueprint.png/256px-001-blueprint.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="512" /></div></div><p> Understand how BEM can help make design decisions throughout all phases of the project.</p><p class="mw-empty-elt"> </p><p class="mw-empty-elt"> </p>\n', '<p> These tutorials show how BEM analysis can support specific design goals in each phase of a project. The design process is presented as a timeline with specific BEM analysis tasks mapped to design tasks performed by architects and engineers during a design project. </p>\n', '</td>\n', '<td style="padding: 20px"><div class="center"><div class="floatnone"><img alt="002-graduation-hat.png" src="/w/images/thumb/5/54/002-graduation-hat.png/128px-002-graduation-hat.png" decoding="async" width="128" height="128" srcset="/w/images/thumb/5/54/002-graduation-hat.png/192px-002-graduation-hat.png 1.5x, /w/images/thumb/5/54/002-graduation-hat.png/256px-002-graduation-hat.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="512" /></div></div><p class="mw-empty-elt"> </p><p> Learn the fundamentals of BEM and the underlying building science principles that are represented in models.</p><p class="mw-empty-elt"> </p><p class="mw-empty-elt"> </p>\n', "<p> These tutorials are not strictly linked to a specific phase of the design process but contribute to practitioners' understanding of how to use BEM effectively. href="#searchInput">Jump to search</a>\n', '\t\t<div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><div class="mw-parser-output"><blockquote><p><b>"Building science</b> is a field of knowledge that draws upon physics, chemistry, engineering, architecture, and the life sciences. Understanding the physical behavior of the building as a system and how this impacts energy efficiency, durability, comfort and indoor air quality is essential to innovating high-performance buildings."\n', '- <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.wbdg.org/resources/building-science-concepts">Whole Building Design Guide</a><sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup></p></blockquote><p>This section is under development and is planned to cover topics such as heating and cooling loads, fundamentals of HVAC systems, energy conservation measures, and others. Refer to the additional resources section below for links to external content.\n', '</p><div id="toc" class="toc" role="navigation" aria-labelledby="mw-toc-heading"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" /><div class="toctitle" lang="en" dir="ltr"><h2 id="mw-toc-heading">Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label class="toctogglelabel" for="toctogglecheckbox"></label></span></div>\n', '<ul>\n', '<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-1"><a href="#Heating_and_Cooling_Loads"><span class="tocnumber">1</span> <span class="toctext">Heating and Cooling Loads</span></a></li>\n', '<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-2"><a href="#HVAC_Fundamentals"><span class="tocnumber">2</span> <span class="toctext">HVAC Fundamentals</span></a></li>\n', '<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-3"><a href="#Energy_and_Other_Metrics"><span class="tocnumber">3</span> <span class="toctext">Energy and Other Metrics</span></a></li>\n', '<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-4"><a href="#Energy_Conservation_Measures"><span class="tocnumber">4</span> <span class="toctext">Energy Conservation Measures</span></a></li>\n', '<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-5"><a href="#Passive_Design"><span class="tocnumber">5</span> <span class="toctext">Passive Design</span></a></li>\n', '<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-6"><a href="#Additional_Resources"><span class="tocnumber">6</span> <span class="toctext">Additional Resources</span></a></li>\n', '<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-7"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">7</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a></li>\n', '</ul>\n', '</div>\n', '\n', '<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Heating_and_Cooling_Loads">Heating and Cooling Loads</span></h2>\n', '<ul><li><b><a href="/wiki/Basics_of_heat_transfer" title="Basics of heat transfer">Basics of heat transfer</a></b> - learn about the three modes of heat transfer: conduction, convection, and radiation.</li>\n', '<li><a href="/wiki/Basics_of_internal_gains" title="Basics of internal gains"><b>Basics of internal gains</b></a> - learn how different sources produce internal gains in a building such as lighting, equipment, and occupants.</li>\n', '<li><a href="/wiki/Fenestration_performance" title="Fenestration performance"><b>Fenestration performance</b></a> - learn about heat transfer through glazed assemblies (windows) and the metrics used to quantify performance.</li>\n', '<li><b><a href="/wiki/Infiltration" title="Infiltration">Infiltration</a></b> - learn how air leakage into and out of the building occurs and how this phenomenon affects the heating and cooling loads.</li></ul>\n', '<p>More content coming soon!\n', '</p>\n', '<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="HVAC_Fundamentals">HVAC Fundamentals</span></h2>\n', '<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Fundamentals_of_HVAC" title="Fundamentals of HVAC"><b>Fundamentals of HVAC</b></a> - a quick primer on key concepts related to HVAC design and operation.</li>\n', '<li><a href="/wiki/HVAC_system_types" title="HVAC system types"><b>HVAC system types</b></a> - detailed descriptions of how systems operate, and how they are represented in simulation software.</li></ul>\n', '<p>More content coming soon!\n', '</p>\n', '<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Energy_and_Other_Metrics">Energy and Other Metrics</span></h2>\n', '<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Site_and_source_energy" title="Site and source energy"><b>Site and source energy</b></a></li>\n', '<li><a href="/wiki/Carbon_and_emission_metrics" title="Carbon and emission metrics"><b>Carbon and emission metrics</b></a></li>\n', '<li>Energy cost</li>\n', '<li>Time dependent valuation</li></ul>\n', '<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Energy_Conservation_Measures">Energy Conservation Measures</span></h2>\n', '<p>Energy conservation measures (ECMs, also commonly referred to as energy efficiency measures - EEMs) are specific design decisions that are made to reduce energy consumption of a particular piece of equipment, or a system as a whole. Most commonly, multiple ECMs are implemented together in an effort to reduce energy consumption to meet a <a href="/wiki/Set_performance_goals_for_the_project" title="Set performance goals for the project">specific goal or target</a>.\n', '</p><p>For a crash course on various energy conservation measures that can be applied to a design project, check out this <a href="/wiki/Energy_Conservation_Measures" title="Energy Conservation Measures">list of ECMs</a>, organized by building system/component.\n', '</p>\n', '<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Passive_Design">Passive Design</span></h2>\n', '<p>Content coming soon!\n', '</p>\n', '<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Additional_Resources">Additional Resources</span></h2>\n', '<ul><li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.heatspring.com/courses/solar-decathlon-building-science-education-series">Solar Decathlon Building Science Education Series</a> - This excellent series of building science education videos was created by the U.S. Department of Energy to support the annual <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.solardecathlon.gov/">Solar Decathlon</a> competition. The series includes primers on how buildings consume energy, zero energy buildings, building envelope, HVAC, lighting, and plug loads. The videos are led by Dr. Paul Torcellini from the <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.nrel.gov">National Renewable Energy Laboratory</a>, and hosted on <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.heatspring.com/">Heatspring</a>, an educational platform focused on topics such as solar, green building, energy efficiency and other technologies. Users must create an account to access the Solar Decathlon videos, but the course is free.</li>\n', '<li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://gard.com/services/energyplus-support-and-training/energyplus-building-physics-modules/">EnergyPlus Building Physics Modules</a> - Presentations and exercises on five building physics topics: Insulation, Thermal Mass, Internal Gains, Infiltration, and Daylighting. Suitable for self-study or for use in a university course. Presentations cover general building physics concepts then show how to model them EnergyPlus. Developed in 2010 by GARD and IIT.</li></ul>\n', '<p><small style="color: gray">Links to external websites are provided as a convenience for further research, but do not imply any endorsement of the content or the operator of the external site, as detailed in BEMcyclopedia\'s <a href="/wiki/Bemcyclopedia:General_disclaimer" title="Bemcyclopedia:General disclaimer">general disclaimers</a>.</small>\n', '</p>\n', '<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span></h2>\n', '<div class="mw-references-wrap"><ol class="references">\n', '<li
